(Rome) Italy has now implemented the increase of its standing army to more than 500,000 men. British Foreign Secretary's Explanation: Four Objectives of Engaging with Germany, Stating This Trip Is Merely Exploratory in Nature; Mission Is of Great Importance, Success or Failure Difficult to Predict 59

Austen Chamberlain to Fly to Berlin Tomorrow

(London) Today, the House of Commons debated German rearmament. Opposition leader Lansbury began by saying that the events of the past week had caused widespread shock and a sense of despair, comparable to 1914. Germany has challenged all nations, demanding the right to tear up the Treaty of Versailles and implement rearmament. This move will inevitably plunge civilization into another devastating war. The Foreign Secretary must not allow Germany to rearm and must declare that the British government's policies are based on armaments, not rearmament. Samuel, leader of the "Samuel Liberal Party," followed, declaring that Austen Chamberlain's mission is extremely difficult. No action should be taken to hinder it. However, the German authorities misunderstand Britain's attitude. Mr. Lansbury's description of the British public's reaction to the German declaration was not overstated. Samuel concluded that Germany should be treated as an equal, but its military superiority cannot be tolerated. This statement was met with cheers in the House. Foreign Secretary Austen Chamberlain replied that he hoped to have sincere discussions with the German Chancellor. This trip must be undertaken with complete sincerity. It is a discussion, not to be preceded by public pronouncements. He and Lord Privy Seal Austen Chamberlain's trip to the continent is exploratory in nature. Austen Chamberlain then quoted the contents of the London Declaration of February 3, stating that Germany had then considered it fair and friendly, and subsequently sent a letter inviting him to visit Berlin. He believed that the scope and purpose of this trip should not be limited to the specific matters listed in the London communiqué. This meeting should thoroughly discuss the main points contained in that communiqué. It is necessary to make this completely clear. This trip has four main objectives: to exchange views on (1) security, (2) armaments, (3) Germany's return to the League of Nations, and (4) a European Air Convention. Germany now only needs to provide assurances that this discussion will be as broad as the one Britain has already communicated to other governments. The above four items are not only proposed, but are in fact the basis for discussion during this visit, so that an agreement can be reached to achieve a final solution. The events of the past week, as Mr. Lansbury has said, naturally aroused protests from the British, French, and Italian governments. What is the appropriate course of action is a serious question. Unilateral action has obviously raised the issue of treaty validity and is also an obstacle to future treaties. He believes that the path the British government wishes to take to deal with this serious situation is relatively appropriate. Refusing to visit Germany or canceling the visit would be of no help. Therefore, the British government requires assurances that the scope of talks will not be limited. Without negotiations and agreements on the above four items to achieve security, the current state of anxiety and panic in Europe cannot be relieved. The British government, having already lodged its reservations and protests in this environment, believes it is necessary and proper to continue this work. He would not comment on the German declaration, but it is appropriate to note that its content and nature are causing concern about the prospects for a common solution. The military strength expressed in the German declaration is enormous, far exceeding the figures put forward a year ago and beyond what the European powers could match a month ago, causing significant concern that Germany's neighbors may not be able to compromise if Germany insists on these figures. He is going to Berlin with the determination to do what Britain can to promote and maintain peace. The aim of British policy has always been to help Germany rejoin the ranks of European nations on fair terms. In any case, European peace must be preserved. The British people do not want to be accused of not doing their utmost to promote peace. We are now working to promote trust among European nations based on firm understanding and general agreement, but we do not wish to conclude special agreements between Britain and any other nation, as the solution must be universal to be solid. (Reuters, 21st)

Austen Chamberlain concluded by saying, "The mission to Germany is very difficult. I dare not say that it will be successful, but to fulfill its due tasks to work for world peace, Britain is undoubtedly responsible." (Havas, 21st)

American Gold Sales Policy: Helping Foreign Countries Restore the Gold Standard? Or Helping Foreign Countries Exchange Silver? 76

(Washington) After Treasury Secretary Morgenthau sold 32,000 ounces of gold to the Mexican Bank yesterday, he stated today that the US government is prepared to sell gold to foreign countries that can offer any conditions. We have already set aside the gold we need, and we will no longer trade for the time being. The Treasury Secretary's words imply that the US government does not want to accumulate gold anymore. Some people on Wall Street believe that this is the government's gesture of willingness to release part of its gold reserves to help foreign countries restore the gold standard, but others believe that the Treasury Department is willing to sell gold and use silver as collateral, which can be seen from Mexico's purchase of gold and sale of silver. However, in any case, there is currently no indication that the United States will redistribute its gold reserves. The Treasury Department stated that the sale of gold to Mexico has no special meaning. (Reuters, 21st)

(Washington) It is certain that the gold sold by the Treasury Department to Mexico and Guatemala was exchanged for silver. After this news was announced, it was rumored today that the United States may also exchange gold for China's silver. Treasury officials declared that the United States is prepared to sell gold to countries in need, and countries can exchange this gold for silver and goods. Therefore, this speculation is becoming increasingly powerful, but officials refused to discuss this issue, only saying that they will sell gold. However, other than Mexico, no negotiations have been conducted with other countries. The responsible parties also recognize that this statement is a preliminary action by the government hoping to complete the reform of the international gold standard, because American gold for silver will expand the scope of gold distribution. The Associated Press learned that the government hopes the world will adopt a new gold standard to stabilize international currencies. This is the original plan of the New Deal. It is said that the development of this matter is particularly noteworthy, because the news that the United States hopes to sell part of its gold was announced by Treasury officials. Treasury officials are concerned about the large increase in gold reserves after the US government stipulated that the gold price is $35 per ounce, for the following reasons: (1) The continuous inflow of gold into the United States will absorb foreign gold reserves. (2) The Treasury Department's huge gold reserves will weaken the power of the United States' 1934 Silver Purchase Act. The United States hopes to implement this law without disturbing the world's financial markets. It is said that since June 1934, the Treasury Department has purchased approximately 400 million ounces of silver. Experts here generally believe that since Canada and China are the main countries supplying silver to the United States, they may be more interested in gold and silver exchanges. According to reports, China raised this issue with the United States last September, but the Chinese Treasury Department's suggestion ultimately did not achieve any success. The revival of this issue will depend on China's final decision on its monetary policy. (National Electric, 21st)

The program for the first official performance tomorrow is the same as today's rehearsal. Tickets for the Mei Lanfang Troupe's performances in Moscow and Leningrad were sold out ten days ago. Therefore, the President of the Soviet Cultural Association, Arosiv, asked Mei to perform in Moscow again after performing in Leningrad. The Cultural Association estimates that there are currently 500,000 people eager to purchase tickets to watch the performance. (Central News Agency Electric, 22nd)

The Plight of Coastal Fishermen in Shandong Province 98

Chen Weixin Visits Han to Discuss Relief Measures

Jinan Correspondence: Shandong's coastal fishing industry has always been known for its development. In recent years, it has suffered aggression from Japanese fishermen and merchants externally and various oppressions internally, leading to gradual decline and a permanent slump. To this day, fishermen along the coasts of Jiaoxian, Zhucheng, Rizhao, Wendeng, Penglai, Fushan, and Huangxian in eastern Shandong are facing extreme hardship and are crying out for food, urgently needing relief. To provide relief to coastal fishermen, Shandong Provincial Chairman Han Fuqu dispatched Provincial Councilor Chen Weixin and others to the coast to investigate the lives of fishermen and the current state of the fishing industry. Chen Weixin left Jinan and went directly to Tao'erbu and Wanggezhuang in Zhucheng County, and Shijiusuo and Taoluozhen in Rizhao for investigation, and then to Lingshanwei and other ports in Jiaoxian for inspection. After ten days of inspections, he visited more than twenty large and small ports. After completing his mission, he returned to Jinan and paid a visit to Provincial Chairman Han Fuqu this afternoon (21st) to report on the plight of coastal fishermen and relief measures. According to Chen Weixin's conversation with the reporter, "I was ordered to go to Jiaoxian, Rizhao, and Zhucheng counties along the coast to investigate the fishing industry. Whenever I arrived at a place, the Public Security Bureau would notify the fishermen to gather for training and to explain Chairman Han's intention to help the fishermen. Therefore, everyone was happy to express their grievances. According to my investigation, the reason for the decline of the fishing industry is that the salt acquisition procedures are too cumbersome. Fishermen must pay a fish tax of three dimes for every hundred catties of fish caught, and then obtain a permit to receive salt. The amount of salt received is estimated based on the size of the boat and the quantity of fish caught, calculated as thirty catties of salt for every hundred catties of fish. Most fishermen are uneducated and elect a carrier to be responsible for receiving salt and selling fish. In recent years, due to the inability to purchase salt, most of the caught fish has been abandoned and rotted. Since we do not have the strength to catch fish, foreign merchants have aggressively fished, leading to the bankruptcy of the fishing industry in this province. Tens of thousands of fishermen have no clothes or food and urgently need relief. The situation is dire. To provide relief, education is of paramount importance, with the establishment of more fishing industry organizations and fishermen's schools to enlighten their knowledge and seek the development of the fishing industry." (21st)

International Commercial Telegram

Reuters Special Commercial Dispatch, March 22nd 99

Gold and Silver

British Gold: London gold prices fell due to the strengthening of the pound, quoted at 146 shillings and 5.5 pence, down 5 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market was very quiet today, with no excitement. The afternoon opening price for spot was 27 pence 1875, and futures were 27 pence 3125, both the same as yesterday's price.

Indian Silver: The Bombay silver market was quiet this morning, with the spot price at 65 rupees 6 annas, followed by a decline. The closing price was 65 rupees 3 annas.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The British pound price rose slightly in the London foreign exchange market. The opening price for British-American exchange was $4.7575, down 375 from yesterday's American-British closing price. It gradually rose afterwards, with the noon price at $4.76875, up 1.125 from the opening price. The price then fell slightly at one o'clock, but rose again at two o'clock to $4.77625, up 1.875 from this morning's opening price.

British-French: The opening price was 72 francs 09, up 6 pounds from yesterday's closing price. It gradually rose afterwards, with the afternoon two o'clock price at 72 francs 46, up 37 pounds from the opening price.

Cotton and Wheat

American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened sluggish, with prices not much changed from yesterday. Prices then fell slightly due to foreign selling, but domestic firms then bought in, and prices recovered slightly.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market opened steady today, but soon turned loose, and prices trended lower due to a lack of buying and the closing out of long positions. Later, due to strong demand for spot goods, Japanese merchants made some purchases, and prices recovered slightly. The closing market situation was quiet. The price of April-May Dijaraj cotton was 218 rupees 25, up 1 rupee 75.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was sluggish today but remained stable. The afternoon one o'clock price for the May term was 6.09, up 1 pound from yesterday's closing price.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market had good sentiment. The afternoon one o'clock price for the May term was 5 shillings and 2 pence.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market rose 1875 at the opening due to weather reports. The Winnipeg wheat market also rose along with prices in the United States and Liverpool.

Rubber

The London rubber market had limited trading. The market price was still stable at the opening, but prices fell back due to few buyers. The noon trading price for the July-September term was 5.5 pence, down 0.0625 from yesterday's closing price.

New York: The New York rubber market also fell today because London prices were not high. There was very little trading, and the market was unexciting.

Securities

New York: Today's Wall Street market was more active than has been seen since the Supreme Court's ruling on the gold clause case. Public utility stocks opened lower. Those holding these securities, mindful of yesterday's rise, sold off at the opening, thereby suppressing the market price. Some fell by one dollar within ten minutes. Later, the selling subsided, and prices recovered slightly. Copper stocks rose due to hopes of an agreement to establish a production reduction agreement at the New York Copper Industry Conference. Sentiment was quite stable, and miners were unwilling to sell at lower prices. Railroad stocks opened slightly lower due to weak business, but only to a limited extent. Within the first hour, a total of 160,000 shares were traded. The prices are as follows:

Northwest Inspection Notes 100

— Special Correspondent of This Newspaper, Geng Ya

Travel Notes on the Return Journey

On the return journey, from Hami to Lanzhou, although revisiting old ground, there were observations not made on the previous trip. A fixed book, even read a hundred times, is never tiresome. The Northwest border region has culture and geography that is largely undeveloped. The teeming masses and myriad things are subject to the rise and fall and extinction and growth as dictated by nature. One does not know how many treasures that have never been discovered there are. Hanyang Pass and Suoyang Ancient City have long been buried in yellow sand and white grass, and people outside the pass commonly say, "Every time you visit there, you are sure to pick up at least one antique, whether it is a brick, a tile, a small Buddha, or a precious tripod, there is no end to it." In other words, not only are Yangguan and Suoyang like this, but almost the entire Northwest border region is like this. Therefore, the most profound feeling gained by this reporter on this trip is that I feel like I have passed through a treasure mountain. Although I do not have a large knife and sharp axe to dig into the mountain and exhaust the rich and beautiful reserves, just looking at the exterior, all the auspicious grasses and strange flowers, the dew-moistened air and refreshing breezes, the lush forests and sparkling sands and stones, the oil gushing from the gullies, and the coal and salt exposed at the foot of the mountains, is enough to make people linger and sway their hearts.

After saying goodbye to the beauty of the Tianshan Mountains, which are covered with eternal snow, and passing through the Xingxing Gorge, with its winding mountains and meandering sand rivers, the Qilian Mountains, which straddle the border of Gansu and Qinghai provinces, also displayed their azure and serene smile, silently welcoming us from hundreds of miles away. The peaks of the Qilian Mountains are also covered with snow, but the color is grayish-white, unlike the bright and clear snow of the Tianshan Mountains, which can be seen from afar. According to observations, the more snow accumulates, the greater the pressure on the lower layers, squeezing out the air, compressing the volume, and at the appropriate freezing point or below, the "regelation phenomenon" transforms it into huge ice blocks. Due to the slope of the mountain and the gravitational pull of the earth, the ice blocks slide down, becoming "glaciers," hanging diagonally in the mountain ravines like hanging silk, the contrast of crystal clear brightness highlights the snow. The snow of the Qilian Mountains mostly does not form glaciers, and if there are any, they can also be used to pan for gold. The Tianshan Mountains are higher than the Qilian Mountains, and all the glaciers are often of unimaginable depth. The speed of glacier movement is extremely slow (the exact details can be known through scientific methods). When the glacier flows to a mountain valley with a higher temperature, the end has an extremely small amount of ice, which melts and drips, forming a water river, but it is not easy to become a large stream, and some are even evaporated. The snow and ice of the Tianshan Mountains mostly disappear into the original mountains, and then flow out into the plains, or are obtained through kaner wells. The scale of water conservancy is also beyond the reach of the Qilian Mountains, which is not just a matter of the brightness of the snow.

It was late winter, and the weather was bitterly cold. At Xingxing Gorge, on the border between Xinjiang and Gansu, on the way we spent the night, it had just snowed, and the wind was especially cold. Because the reporter wanted to catch the Anxi merchant convoy's car, I especially prepared four horses, and the horse owner and I each rode one, and the other two horses carried food and supplies (there was nowhere to buy them along the way after the soldiers burned it). We pressed on and advanced at the same time, setting out at dawn and not lodging until sunset. The Xingxing Gorge station is a large station consisting of two consecutive ninety-li sections. By the time we arrived, it was already after the second watch. There were no inns or homes. I entered the Guandi Temple and knocked on the postman's door to ask for lodging. In response, I learned that the person inside was not a postman, but a clerk registering postal items between Gansu and Xinjiang. He claimed that he had just finished "quietly sitting down Dan," and feared being blown by the cold wind, he only passed out the kitchen key and matches from the window seam, instructing us to open the door and cook. There were bowls, chopsticks, pots, and pans in the kitchen, as well as camel dung for fuel, but the empty jar had no water. I went out of the temple to look for a well but could not find it, and there was no one else to guide me, so I had to melt the snow in the courtyard to water the horses and filter it to cook noodles. After eating, there were faint traces of wash water on the bottom of the bowl, which froze after being placed on the table for a moment. Only then did I realize that the empty jar did not store water to prevent freezing and damaging it. The next morning, while still drowsy, I suddenly felt a slight warmth on my face. I opened my eyes and saw the horse owner carrying a lit candle, approaching the bedside. The candlelight gently illuminated my face, and I immediately felt a slight warmth. How cold the night air was could be inferred from this. The four horses were tied to the exposed trough pillars, and their exhalations condensed into frost on their lips and fur. The old horse even dripped saliva that turned into ice, intersecting like canine teeth. Later, the postman got up and led us to pick up crystals and star stones, and pointed out the location of the coal mine. As we walked and talked, he said that his name was Wang Yinglie, from Shandong, and that he had joined the Tongshanshe. He had come to this uninhabited place to find this leisurely job, so as to rest. As he spoke, his hands trembled and his head shook constantly. I asked him if he had been greatly frightened or stimulated. He replied that Mr. Hedin and his party had stayed here before, and someone else had also said that he had phlegm. In fact, "If virtue is one foot tall, the devil is ten feet tall." He had gotten this illness because of sitting quietly. I then asked him since he knew the source of the illness, why didn't he stop sitting quietly, but he did not answer. At that time, a wild horse fled in fright, so he turned to other topics and said that there were many wild horses, foxes, wolves, and rabbits here. It was very interesting to climb up high in the morning to watch them. Some wild horses are tamed by hunters, but their backs are soft and cannot be ridden.

Upon arriving in Anxi, just as I took the saddle off my horse, an old friend told me that my previous visit to Anxi had caused a great disaster for the people of Anxi. Shocked, I asked the reason. My friend said, "In your Northwest Inspection Notes, you briefly mentioned Anxi's production of native salt. After the Gansu Salt Transport Bureau read the newspaper, it immediately telegraphed the Anxi County Magistrate, ordering him to quickly provide a detailed report, with the intention of setting up a bureau to collect taxes. This native salt is produced far away in Caohu, and its quality and color are poor. Only a few extremely poor Mongolian people reluctantly use it to make water to add flavor. It is not worthy to be called edible salt. Previously, the neighboring Dunhuang and Yumen counties were also discovered by the Salt Bureau to produce some native salt, and at first, special commissioners were sent to collect it, but in the end, the income did not cover the expenses, so it was changed to be collected by the county government as an additional tax. Regardless of whether the farmers sell salt or not, and whether they can afford salt or not, they must be assessed and pay the tax uniformly every quarter. To this day, the local people suffer from this. Moreover, Anxi originally had nine hundred households, but because of evading heavy taxes, there are now only a little over five hundred households left. If salt tax is imposed again, the people of Anxi will have no way out," and so on. Wherever the reporter goes, I must ask about the local specialties and tell the people of the country, intending to arouse the attention of all parties, to study development and improvement, in order to make the best use of the geographical advantages. I never thought that it would cause trouble, causing the local people to worry about possessing a treasure. This is truly regrettable and was not something I had anticipated.

Xiamen Huge Robbery Case 101

The Japanese-owned Fengnan Company robbed of over 30,000 yuan; Chinese and Japanese detectives conduct a massive search, apprehending five suspects

Xiamen Dispatch: Recently, robbery cases have occurred in busy areas of Xiamen. On the 19th at noon, the Japanese-owned Fengnan Trust Company on Zhenbang Road was the site of a huge robbery of over 20,000 yuan, and a police officer named Zhang Baosheng was shot and killed. The entire city of Xiamen was shocked after the incident. Wang Gu Pan, the director of the Xiamen Public Security Bureau, immediately dispatched all detectives and police to mobilize and rigorously pursue the criminals. The Japanese Consulate also ordered all Japanese detectives to cooperate in the pursuit. The situation is extremely tense. The details are recorded as follows:

Zhenbang Road is located behind Haihou Nan Road and, along with Haihou and Chenguang Roads, is a gathering place for banks, money shops, and foreign firms, making it the most prosperous central market in Xiamen. The Fengnan Trust Company, located at No. 48, is operated by Taiwanese Japanese and is adjacent to the Zhongnan Bank. It has a capital of 200,000 yuan and is invested in by wealthy Taiwanese merchants. The manager, Lin Mutu, is Taiwanese. The business is very prosperous, being the largest money business in Xiamen run by Taiwanese. In addition to trust business, it also engages in remittance, advance, and other businesses. Recently, due to the brisk sales of Japanese goods in southern Fujian, remittance and advance to Taiwan are extremely developed, surpassing even the Xiamen branch of the Bank of Taiwan. On the 19th, as the Osaka regular ship Fengshan Maru was scheduled to depart for Taiwan, there were a large number of people withdrawing money and making remittances, making the business twice as busy as usual. At 12:10 PM, Manager Lin Mutu and more than a dozen clerks were in the midst of handling the overwhelming business when a man in a Western-style suit and black overcoat arrived. He sat on the long bench where customers usually sat. Soon, several more people entered, all wearing black or dark blue overcoats. However, the weather was extremely hot that day, and they were all wearing overcoats, which was quite unusual. But they were still assumed to be customers and were not paid much attention. At that moment, one person approached the counter, claiming to buy a ship ticket and remit funds. As the clerk turned to get the ticket, the man had already jumped over the counter. The others wearing overcoats also pressed forward, all taking out handguns from inside their coats. The remaining robbers entered the counter, two of them keeping watch for any outcry, two guarding the door, and the rest monitoring the cashier, Wang Yan, and the accounting clerk, Lü Zhenfang. Six robbers searched and robbed, first forcing Lin to hand over the key to the iron safe. They could not open it, so they forced Lin to open it himself. The safe had two layers. The first layer contained mortgage documents. The robbers took one envelope, opened it, and saw that it was a real estate deed. They discarded it without regard. The second layer contained money, but they did not know there was a second layer and did not open it. So, they robbed the cash and banknotes on the counter. At that time, business was busy with receipts and deposits, and over 10,000 yuan in banknotes from various banks, including the Bank of China, Central Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Industrial Bank, and Communications Bank, were completely robbed. At that time, a bundle of five-yuan banknotes, totaling 18 bundles or 9,000 yuan, was delivered from the Bank of Communications. In addition, Japanese gold notes worth 1,250 yuan were also robbed. After the robbery, they drove Lin and the clerks, along with the customers, into the toilet on the left side of the rear, cut the telephone line, and left together through the main entrance. After the robbers exited, one of the clerks followed and shouted "Robbers!" The robbers immediately opened fire as a warning. The clerk then fell silent and retreated. Coincidentally, Zhang Baosheng, a police officer from the 2nd Security Team of the Public Security Bureau, was checking the post on behalf of the squad leader and arrived in front of the Zhongnan Bank when he suddenly heard gunshots and saw several people with guns rushing out of Fengnan. Knowing it was a robbery, but Zhang was on patrol and not carrying a weapon, he asked two auxiliary police officers at the Zhongnan Bank to lend him their two Mauser pistols to help chase the robbers. The two auxiliary police officers refused. Zhang then followed the robbers. At that time, there were ten robbers. Three of them escaped separately, and the remaining seven robbers entered Shipihu Lane, passing through Buda Street and the Grandmother Temple. Zhang followed closely. When the robbers reached Dazhong Road, they split up again, four robbers fleeing towards Siming West Road and three towards Tuqi. Zhang then abandoned the pursuit towards Siming West Road and followed those towards Tuqi. The three robbers saw Zhang following closely and, as they approached Wutong Dam, Zhang was only a dozen paces away from the robbers. He heard a robber curse Zhang in the Xiamen dialect and, realizing the danger, quickly dodged. The robbers had already opened fire, firing three shots in a row, hitting Zhang in the left buttock and passing through his left thigh. He immediately fell to the ground wounded. At the same time, a 14-year-old boy named Wang Gan, a passerby, was also injured.

After the robbers left, Fengnan immediately borrowed a telephone to report to the Third Division of the Public Security Bureau and the Japanese Police Sub-Station of the Japanese Consulate. Liu Handong, the director of the Detective Division, Yi Jingjian, the chief of the Third Division, and Xie Shaozeng, the chief of the Public Security Bureau of Siming County, rushed to investigate one after another. Kamine, the chief of the Japanese Police Sub-Station of the Japanese Consulate in Xiamen, accompanied by Watanabe, the chief of the Judicial Affairs Section, and Sano, the chief of the section, also led Japanese detectives to investigate. Immediately, both the Chinese and Japanese sides dispatched police officers, along with clerks from Fengnan, to set out separately and conduct a thorough search in brothels, opium dens, civilian residences, and various bus stations, as well as the Fengshan Maru and Fengqing Lun, which were scheduled to depart that day. At 6 PM, two suspects, Pan Damu and Pan Ertong, were apprehended. Later, it was found that they were shop assistants at the Huaide Residence on Zhenbang Road and were released as they were not involved. That night, a Taiwanese man named Cai Gancao, who was carrying a pistol, was apprehended at a Taiwanese opium den at No. 55 Shuixian Road. He was taken back by the Japanese police for interrogation. On the 21st, Chinese and Japanese detectives continued to guard the main streets and search, including on various departing ships and even the residences of major Taiwanese figures. However, nothing was found. In the evening, according to a tip from an informant, a Taiwanese man named Huang Shuitu, who worked at the Shui Ji Trading Company at Houlutou, was involved in the Fengnan robbery. Someone had seen Huang and two others fleeing from Tuqi, and Huang had squatted down and wrapped banknotes in a towel. The Japanese police immediately went to the address to arrest Huang and two of his shop assistants. Huang vehemently denied it. However, his shop assistants claimed that Huang had gone out at 11 AM that morning and returned to the shop around 12 noon. They had seen him and a gambling house clerk wrapping something unknown in newspaper. After interrogation, they were temporarily detained. Furthermore, at Li Zongjiu's residence at No. 14 Guangping Lane, Li and a Taiwanese man named Chen Jinzhi were arrested. Around 11 PM, two Taiwanese men named Huang Shuisheng and Zhang Dingyuan were arrested at the Anda Hotel on Siming West Road. Over a hundred yuan in banknotes were found on Huang's person. The Japanese police took them away for interrogation. All five are suspected, and the case has not yet been solved.

Wang Gu Pan, the Director of the Xiamen Special Public Security Bureau, was extremely angered by the occurrence of this case. Since robbery cases had occurred mostly within the jurisdiction of the Third Division, and the Fengnan robbery case was also within the jurisdiction of that division, he immediately ordered the dismissal of Yi Jingjian, the chief of the Third Division, and transferred Wang Zhengju to succeed him as the chief of the Third Division, with a strict deadline to solve the case. (March 21st)

Jiujiang: Commerce Declining Daily 102

562 Businesses Closed in Five Years

Nanchang Correspondence: Jiujiang is one of China's Yangtze River trading ports and the gateway for imports and exports of Jiangxi. In recent years, the decline of Xunbu's commerce and finance has been rapid. According to the Statistics Office of the Provincial Government, from the 18th to the 22nd year of the Republic of China, the money industry decreased by 18 firms, the egg and timber industries decreased by 9 firms, the cotton industry decreased by 12 firms, the grain industry decreased by 49 firms, the porcelain industry decreased by 26 firms, the charcoal industry decreased by 30 firms, the Jiangsu and Zhejiang foreign goods industry decreased by 19 firms, the oil, salt, and sundry goods industry decreased by 43 firms, the rice industry decreased by 55 firms, and customs declaration and transshipment warehouses decreased by 27 firms. In total, the number of new businesses in various industries in five years was only 67, while the total number of closed businesses reached 562. Comparing the two, there was a net decrease of 495 firms. The decline of commerce is truly alarming. Even in terms of finance, although on the surface it seems that the number of banks is increasing daily, it is also because of the bankruptcy of the rural economy, with cash concentrating in urban areas. Due to the decline of industry and commerce, the deposits received cannot be lent out, forming a phenomenon of "cerebral hemorrhage and withered limbs." The future is difficult to be optimistic about. Moreover, since the Republic of China, imports have gradually increased sharply in the province, and exports by the 20th year of the Republic of China, the trade deficit reached over 20 million Haikwan taels. If such a large amount of cash outflow is not urgently addressed, there will eventually be a day of exhaustion. (3/18)

Songjiang: Civil Affairs Department Punishes Public Security Personnel 103

Li Zehuan, the chief of the First Branch of the Public Security Bureau in Tinglin Town, Songjiang County, was previously accused by the people of having no achievements after serving for a year and of accepting bribes and conniving with drug offenders. After the Civil Affairs Department sent someone to secretly investigate and found the accusations to be true, Director Yu personally approved the dismissal and detention of the branch chief, Li Zehuan. He Yongyao, the director of the bureau, was found to have failed to investigate properly and was given a major demerit in accordance with the regulations for joint responsibility for the appointment of public security personnel.

Jiading: Dispute over Inheritance Leads to Murder 104

Zhu Shouli and Zhu Liren, farmers in Wujia Village southwest of Malu Town, have been involved in lawsuits for many years due to disputes over inheriting the estate of a relative. Their resentment was deep. On the 14th of this month, another dispute over inheritance led to a verbal argument, followed by a physical fight. Shouli's youngest son, Xiaodi, injured Liren's head. Liren went to the county seat that day to have the injury examined and died on the morning of the 18th due to the severity of the injury. After the family reported the death, County Magistrate Xu went to the village on the 20th to examine the body. Because Liren had no children, his body remains uncoffined to this day. The murderer, Zhu Xiaodi, has been apprehended and detained.

Suzhou: Request to Reduce Electricity Rates Reaches a Stalemate 105

The various silk weaving industries in Suzhou, in order to request a reduction in motor electricity rates, dispatched representatives Liu Fuqing, Lu Jigao, and She Wenqing to Beijing to petition the Central Construction Committee. This has already been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that after the representatives petitioned, they returned to Suzhou yesterday (the 22nd). It is said that the motor electricity rate has been reduced from 8.5 fen per kilowatt-hour to 6 fen, which should be no problem. The base price of the motor electricity meter is 1.4 yuan per meter. Large users suffer only limited losses, but small users suffer significant losses, which has not been resolved. The electricity rate for lamps is 2 jiao per kilowatt-hour. Users proposed to change it to 1.8 jiao, but the factory has not agreed. Therefore, the various industries are deeply dissatisfied and have submitted a petition to the county party headquarters, requesting permission to organize the Suzhou Electricity Users Association. The party headquarters is currently deliberating.

Songjiang Prison Warden Suspended and Placed Under Surveillance 106

Zhu Shusheng, the president of the Jiangsu Higher Court, received a report that prisoners in Songjiang County Jail suddenly broke free from their fetters around 5 PM on the 18th of this month and rushed out, cutting the telephone lines in the warden's office and tying up the guards. Fourteen prisoners escaped at the same time. President Zhu was enraged and specifically telegraphed the county magistrate of Songjiang County yesterday (the 22nd), ordering that the prison warden, Li Shuzhang, be suspended and placed under surveillance and handed over to the County Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation and legal proceedings.

Wuxi: Trial of Yixing County Magistrate's Case to Begin 107

Gu Tongsun, the former director of land tax in Yixing County, and his younger brother, Gu Kangsun, were detained for corruption but suddenly escaped. Chu Kaiyao, the judicial secretary of the county, had acted as Gu's guarantor and, fearing punishment, also fled. Zhong Jingcheng, the county magistrate, detained Chu's wife, Shao, for questioning, causing her injuries. Chu's family sent telegrams to appeal. The Jiangsu Higher Court ordered Qian Chengjun, the chief prosecutor of the local branch court, to go to Yixing to examine the injury and investigate. At the same time, Gu Tianzhen's wife, Gu Wang, accused County Magistrate Zhong of abuse. The Jiangsu Higher Court also ordered Ren Guanghai, an inspecting officer from the local branch court of Wuxi, to go to Yixing to investigate. Both cases were reported to the Jiangsu Higher Court for review. The Jiangsu Higher Court has now designated the local branch court of Wuxi to have jurisdiction over the above two cases and has sent all case files for review. Upon receiving the order, Chief Qian of Wuxi will soon issue warrants to summon the original defendants, Chu Shao, Gu Wang, and Zhong Jingcheng, to appear in court for investigation in accordance with the law.

Audit Office Dispatches Commissioners for Secret Investigation of Accusation Case 108

Chen Gongliang, a section chief from the Audit Office of the Ministry of Finance, arrived in Wuxi from Shanghai the night before and stayed in room number one at the Washington Hotel. He departed at 8 AM yesterday to investigate in various places. It is said that someone had accused the tax police of harassment in Wuxi to the Audit Office. Zhu Tingqi, the director and acting chief of the Office, dispatched him to Wuxi for secret investigation.

Nantong: Zhao Dihua and Zhu Ping Visit Nantong for Inspection 109

Zhao Dihua, the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance, and Zhu Ping, the Director of the Land Bureau, visited Nantong on the 20th to inspect and resolve the case of corruption in land tax collection. In the afternoon, they inspected the collapse of the riverbank on the south side and were hosted by local gentry, including Chen Hechu, to visit Langshan. At the Sanyuan Temple, they viewed the Ming edition of the Tripitaka. At 4 PM on the 21st, people from all walks of life held a welcome meeting at the Nantong Theater, presided over by Commissioner Zheng. Zhao spoke about the administrative policy of Jiangsu Province, and Zhu spoke about the significance of land reform. At 7 PM in the evening, people from all walks of life held a public banquet at the club. Zhao and Zhu originally intended to go to the coastal areas of San Yu and Lüsi to inspect the reclamation and salt areas, but were unable to do so due to the snow. They left for Shanghai that night and then went to Zhenjiang.

Changzhou: Detailed Report of the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Joint Meeting in Changzhou 110

The Standing Committee meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce was held at the Changzhou Chamber of Commerce around 3 PM on the 21st. Fourteen people attended, including Yu Xiaochuan, Qian Sunqing, and Cheng Ganqing. Yu Xiaochuan chaired the meeting. The rituals were performed as usual. Reporting items (omitted). Discussion items: (1) The chambers of commerce of Yixing, Zhenjiang, Wujin, Wuxi, Qingpu, Gaoyou, and Fengxian successively sent letters and telegrams stating that the Provincial Government meeting on February 26 passed the regulations for collecting house donations in various counties of the province and requested that reasonable arguments be made to the Provincial Government to stop the implementation because of the difficulties of the people in Jiangsu, etc. After a letter was sent to the Provincial Donation and Tax Supervision Committee suggesting that the Provincial Government should quickly stop the implementation, a reply was received that the meeting had two opinions and suggested that the Provincial Government investigate and handle the matter accordingly. Should the Chamber continue to appeal? It was resolved that the Chamber would summarize the opinions of the chambers of commerce of various counties, truthfully submit them, and request a stop to the implementation in order to alleviate the difficulties of the people in Jiangsu and avoid disturbances. (2) The Rugao County Chamber of Commerce and the Rugao County Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Office telegraphed to report a dispute over spot checks of stamp tax and requested an investigation and handling. How should this case be handled? It was resolved that since both parties had filed lawsuits separately, they should quietly await the judicial authorities to investigate and handle the matter. (3) The Wuxian and Wujin County Chambers of Commerce proposed that the new stamp tax law newly formulated by the Ministry of Finance has not yet been promulgated. During this transition period between the old and new laws, merchants are prone to misunderstandings. It is requested that the new law be promulgated as soon as possible and that inspections be temporarily suspended before the new law is promulgated to avoid disturbances. At the same time, the new stamp tax law should be promulgated as soon as possible. Please vote for the resolution. It was resolved to pass. (4) The Wuxian Chamber of Commerce and other six groups launched a memorial meeting for Mr. Shi Yunqing. Please include the Chamber's name as a sponsor and forward it to the chambers of commerce of various counties and towns to participate. The resolution was passed. (5) After inquiring about the qualifications of alternate members of the Chamber of Commerce, the Ministry and Province ordered the transfer of the resolution of the Unified Legislation Conference to the Chamber. Since Mr. Yuan Zhensheng, a member of the Executive Committee of the Chamber, was vacant due to illness in August of last year, should he be re-elected in accordance with this explanation? Please vote for the resolution. It was resolved that Xu Yao, an alternate member of the Executive Committee, should be re-elected. (6) The Yixing County Chamber of Commerce proposed that the business tax rate for oil and sauce be changed to three levels, collecting 2/1000. Oil and sauce are daily necessities for the people. At this time of rural collapse and overall social and economic upheaval, the people are truly unable to bear it. It is requested to submit a request to continue to tax the oil and sauce tax rate at 2/1000 as before in order to maintain the food of the people and relieve the difficulties of merchants. It was resolved to investigate and handle the case as appropriate. (7) The Chamber's income and expenditure report for January should be submitted to the Supervisory Committee for review. The resolution was passed.

Danyang: Conflict Between River Workers and Security Team Soldiers 111

Due to the impact of the drought in the past year, the counties south of the Yangtze River in Jiangsu Province suffered severe droughts, with thousands of miles of barren land and no harvest. The livelihood of farmers was completely cut off. In order to relieve the people in the disaster areas, the government, in addition to raising and distributing emergency relief, also had the act of hiring laborers to dredge the canal. The laws, beauty, intention, and goodness need not be mentioned. Since the start of the work, nearly 20,000 laborers recruited in Jintan County have been assigned to work on various sections along the canal, which has been quite active. However, what one person makes each day is not enough for one person to eat each day. The misery can be imagined. Therefore, the laborers often complain. The security team soldiers stationed in Erling Town, Danyang, were ordered to protect the workers. Suddenly, they had a conflict with the laborers. Yesterday (the 19th) afternoon, the guards suddenly arrested two labor foremen, Li and Qian. When the laborers found out, they gathered at the security team's garrison to question them. Li Zhenyu, the captain of the team, was unable to answer. The labor foremen wanted to rush into the garrison. Seeing this, the security team soldiers immediately raised their guns and fired at the workers as a show of self-defense. (?) As a result, a laborer named Dai Jinxu was killed on the spot, and several laborers, including Chen, were injured. The crowd was enraged for a time. The security team soldiers, seeing that they had caused a major disaster, quickly took the two labor foremen, Li and Qian, and the team back to the Fifth Brigade Headquarters in Danyang, claiming that the laborers had rioted, robbed firearms, and kidnapped a soldier named Li Yunduan. The county magistrate and commander of the Fifth Brigade immediately telegraphed the county magistrate of Jinhuai County, Qi Lunjie, to jointly inspect the scene of the incident in order to find a proper solution. However, after all the dredging laborers learned of this incident, they all went on strike, which had a significant impact on the project. There is still no news of a resolution.

Hangzhou: Zhejiang Province Begins to Implement Spring Relief 112

The autumn drought in Zhejiang Province was severe, affecting more than forty counties and a large number of victims. In addition to allocating 250,000 yuan for winter relief in January, which has been completely distributed, the provincial government has now allocated 350,000 yuan for spring relief. After a meeting of the Relief Affairs Committee, 70,000 yuan was allocated to the Shanghai Jiaxu Zhejiang Relief Association for distribution, and the remaining 280,000 yuan was properly distributed according to the severity of the disaster in various counties as follows: 13,000 yuan for Yuqian, 12,000 yuan for Changshan, 16,000 yuan for Kaihua, 13,000 yuan for Lin'an, 16,000 yuan for Jiande, 10,000 yuan for Tiantai, 5,000 yuan for Wuxing, 15,000 yuan for Changxing, 10,000 yuan for Xiaofeng, 14,000 yuan for Tonglu, 13,000 yuan for Fenshui, 10,000 yuan for Xindeng, 12,000 yuan for Fuyang, 14,000 yuan for Pujiang, 5,000 yuan for Zhuji, 16,000 yuan for Chun'an, 14,000 yuan for Shouchang, 10,000 yuan for Xianju, 11,000 yuan for Yunhe, 13,000 yuan for Changhua, 22,000 yuan for Jiangshan. The above twenty counties totaled 280,000 yuan for relief. The Relief Association also telegraphed each county to send personnel to the province to discuss the distribution method. It is planned to purchase food with part of the relief funds to facilitate the simultaneous distribution of food and funds. It can be started in a few days.

Local News

Asahi Visiting Aircraft Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday; Japanese Consul-General Holds Tea Party at 4 PM; Japan Press Association Hosts Banquet at 7 PM 115

Scheduled to Depart for Japan at 6 AM Tomorrow Morning

According to the Central News Agency, the "Asahi 110," a visiting aircraft from the Asahi Shimbun Company of Tokyo and Osaka, Japan, specially permitted by our government and piloted by Hyakuzo Shinno and Kenji Tsukagoshi, arrived in Nanjing at 5:30 PM on the 20th. There, they paid respects at the mausoleum, visited various government officials, and attended a welcome banquet hosted by the press. Yesterday, they departed from Nanjing at 12:37 PM and arrived in Shanghai at 1:52 PM, landing at Longhua Airport. The Shanghai Municipal Government specially prepared a welcome reception at the airport. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Japanese Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi, and others personally welcomed them, with hundreds in attendance. At 4 PM, the Japanese Consul-General held a tea party. At 7 PM, the Japan Press Association hosted a banquet. The aircraft is scheduled to depart for Japan at 6 AM on the 24th. Details are as follows:

Reception Venue Arrangement Beforehand, the Municipal Government sent personnel to erect two welcome arches at the airport. Inside the hangar, hundreds of seats were arranged for refreshments. Large Chinese and Japanese national flags were hung on the walls. Countless Party and national flags were crisscrossed on the seats. To maintain order, anyone without an entrance pass or car pass was prohibited from entering the second gate. The Public Security Bureau band played music to welcome the visitors.

Welcoming Personnel From yesterday noon, the road leading to Longhua Airport was lined with vehicles. Security personnel guarded the route. In addition to Mayor Wu Tiecheng, the Chinese side included Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun, Section Chief Li Dachao, Secretaries Zhang Tingrong and Tang Shixuan, Specialist Wang Changchun, Councilor Jin from the Garrison Headquarters, Deputy Adjutant-General Gan, Shanghai Security Bureau Director Yang Hu, Public Security Bureau Chief Inspector Huang, North Station Branch Director Liang Fuchu, Director Yu Ming and Secretary Zhou Jue of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, and Yao Xijiu of the Chinese Aviation Association. On the Japanese side were Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi, First Secretary Horiuchi of the Japanese Embassy, Chinese Affairs Secretary Arino, Army Assistant Officer Itta, Navy Assistant Officer Kobetto, Information Department Chief Ashino Hiroshi, Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai Ishii Jutaro, and Chairman of the Japanese Chamber of Commerce, Yoneri, among hundreds of others. Japanese men, women, and elementary school students made up more than half of the welcoming crowd, waving Chinese and Japanese national flags to show their welcome. Dai Enji, manager of China National Aviation Corporation, oversaw all arrangements on site.

Landing Details At 1:47 PM, the "Asahi 110" was spotted in the northeastern sky. It landed three minutes later, slowly taxiing to the reception area. Pilots Shinno and Tsukagoshi leaned out of the cockpit window and saluted the welcoming crowd to the sound of military music. After the aircraft stopped, personnel from the Public Security Bureau conducted a detailed inspection in accordance with foreign aircraft entry regulations. Both pilots were in high spirits. Upon disembarking, they were immediately surrounded by Chinese and foreign reporters for photographs and film footage. The aircraft is a monoplane, painted grass green, with the Asahi logo under the wings. It is a semi-locally made Japanese aircraft manufactured in February of Showa 9 (1934), with one 600-horsepower engine and a top speed of 270 miles per hour. It also carried three letters of greeting to the Mayor of Shanghai and the citizens from the mayors of Tokyo and Osaka, and the presidents of the two Asahi Shimbun companies.

Grand Welcome Mayor Wu and others shook hands with both pilots one by one, exchanging brief greetings. Miss Liang Xue'er and Miss Liang Xueji then stepped forward to present flowers. Several Japanese women also represented Japanese Consul-General Ishii Jutaro, the Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun, the Shanghai Japanese Reporters' Association, the Shanghai Resident Association, and the Banzai Hall, presenting fresh flowers or paper flowers. They were then led into the reception area, where Mayor Wu presided over a welcome meeting, with light refreshments and yellow wine.

Mayor's Speech At the welcome reception, Mayor Wu said in his address, "Distinguished guests, Mr. Shinno, Mr. Tsukagoshi, today the Tokyo and Osaka Asahi Shimbun's aircraft has flown to China and landed in our city. As the local host, I extend a warm welcome on behalf of the entire city to your company's goodwill in sending this aircraft to visit China. I also express my deep respect and appreciation for the spirit of Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi who piloted this aircraft. The progress of transportation is indeed an important factor in promoting world politics, and the development of aviation can break through many natural and material obstacles in the universe, increasing opportunities for mutual assistance and cooperation among various ethnic groups, and even eliminate various spiritual barriers between ethnic groups, and improve international relations between them. Our two countries, China and Japan, have a very long and close relationship in history and geography. Our cultures and institutions, our customs and habits, are not only related to each other, but also not far apart. They can indeed be said to be two brotherly countries of the same culture and the same race. Recently, Sino-Japanese diplomatic relations have gradually shown signs of improvement, which is truly gratifying. We are especially grateful for the kindness of your aircraft's visit to China. Today, we respectfully accept the goodwill brought by your aircraft. At the same time, we sincerely hope that your aircraft can bring to your country the spirit of the kingly way of culture that the Chinese nation has cherished for thousands of years, which values faith and peace, and, through your newspaper, which is the most authoritative in your country's public opinion, spread this spirit widely to your compatriots, so as to completely eliminate the spiritual barriers between the two brotherly countries and increase the belief in the coexistence and co-prosperity of the two nations. I wish your aircraft a safe return journey, and I wish Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi good health."

Japanese Response Following this, Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai Ishii Jutaro delivered a speech, saying in essence, "We are very grateful for the grand reception given to the Asahi aircraft's visit to your country. We are especially pleased that this will enhance goodwill between China and Japan." Next, Mr. Kamio Shigeru, Director of the Eastern Department of the Tokyo and Osaka Asahi Shimbun, spoke, saying, "In the Sui and Tang Dynasties, it took a month for a journey between China and Japan, which was extremely inconvenient, so there was little interaction in diplomatic relations. Although there has been great progress now, compared to the dense network of air routes between European and American countries, the convenience and speed of travel are quite backward. Therefore, we sincerely hope that East Asia can catch up quickly to seek progress." Finally, pilot Shinno answered, translated by Wang Changchun, saying, "This time, I piloted the aircraft from Tokyo via Osaka and Korea, arriving in Nanjing the day before yesterday and arriving in Shanghai today. This new route is related to both China and Japan. We are very grateful for the banquet given by your country's authorities in Nanjing. After arriving in Shanghai, we received a warm welcome from the Mayor and all sectors of society, which almost brought tears to my eyes. We are scheduled to fly back on the original aircraft at 6 AM the day after tomorrow (tomorrow). We sincerely hope that this trip will strengthen the relationship between Shanghai and Osaka and make it closer, and report your country's enthusiasm to the whole country. Thank you."

Japanese Consul's Tea Party After the welcome ceremony, Japanese Consul-General accompanied Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi to the consulate, and then to the Banzai Hall on Seymour Road for a short rest. At 4 PM, Japanese Consul-General Ishii Jutaro held a tea party at his private residence on Seymour Road to entertain the two pilots and guests from all walks of life. Attendees included Section Chief Li Dachao and Secretary Tang Shixuan of the Municipal Government, Shanghai Security Bureau Director Yang Hu, Yu Ming of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Haian, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Chairman Yu Zuoting, banking leaders Lin Kanghou and Dian Shoumin, and prominent figures Du Yuesheng and Zhang Xiaolin, as well as Japanese officers, and Chinese and foreign press, totaling about 200 people. The Ishii couple hosted the event, and several young Japanese women served tea and refreshments. The guests chatted and laughed happily. Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi were especially welcomed by the guests. The Chinese Aviation Association also presented a pair of antique vases, inscribed with the words "Magnificent Flight," which lasted until 6 PM.

Press Association Banquet The Shanghai Press Association hosted a banquet at the Xinghualou Restaurant on Fuzhou Road at 8 PM last night. On the host side were Wang Boqi, Zhou Mengxiong, Wu Tingchen, Yu Songhua, Ma Yinliang, Qian Bohan, Qian Hua, Wang Shenwei, Li Haoran, Yan Duhe, Wang Weizhen, Zhu Yinong, Yao Junyu, Lu Yi, Wang Jilu, Lai Guangfu, Shao Jizhi, Pan Gongbi, Xiong Shaohao, Xiang Yuancun, Zheng Xitao, Pan Gongzhan, He Xiya, Xiu Fang, Xu Zhuodai, Guan Ji'an, Qian Cangshuo, Yuan Yeyu, Lin Baisheng, Ye Xuesong, Zhao Muru, Guo Xiufeng, and Xu Xinyi. The guests of honor were Asahi aircraft pilots Hyakuzo Shinno and Kenji Tsukagoshi, and Kamio Shigeru, Director of the Eastern Department of the Asahi Shimbun. Accompanying guests were Kinoshita Moriyama, Imai, and Kurai of the Asahi Shimbun; Tachibana and Murakami of the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun; Shimojo and Ishida of the Dentsu News Agency; Matsumoto and Zhuangyuan of the Nihon Rengo Tsushin; Akakami of the Tokyo Jiji Shinpo; Otsuki of the Hochi Shimbun; Ishikawa and Ito of the Nichinichi Shimbun; Hada and Goto of the Shanghai Nichiho; Fukamachi and Otorii of the Shanghai Nichinichi Shimbun; and Yamada Gisaburo of the Shanghai Weekly. Halfway through the banquet, the chairman, Mr. Wang Boqi, General Manager of the Xinwenbao, delivered a welcome speech, which was translated by Mr. Hu Yizang, saying, "I am very honored to represent the Shanghai Press Association today to welcome Mr. Hyakuzo Shinno and Mr. Kenji Tsukagoshi of the Tokyo and Osaka Asahi Shimbun who have flown to visit the Republic of China. The Shanghai and other local press colleagues are all envious of the two gentlemen's sea crossing and long-distance visit. We have always known that your country's newspapers are progressing rapidly, and all the scales and equipment are sufficient for our country's newspapers to emulate. Now that Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi, representing the most advanced Tokyo and Osaka Asahi Shimbun in Japan, have come to visit our country, all of us in the press hope that you will give us more instruction and serve as a reference for our country's newspapers. At the same time, we feel that the development of the press must rely on the progress of transportation, and the aviation industry has a great contribution to the transmission of information and the delivery of newspapers for the press. Now, the Asahi Shimbun can provide its own aircraft to travel to our country, which shows the perfection of the equipment, and today's safe arrival in Shanghai, we can gather together, which shows the talent of the flight technicians, which really makes us admire very much. Now, I would like to propose a toast, wishing the Asahi Shimbun's development, the health of the two gentlemen, and please the two gentlemen not to hesitate to give us advice."

Japanese Guests' Response After Mr. Wang finished his speech, Mr. Hyakuzo Shinno stood up to reply, translated by Yamada Gisaburo, saying, "I am very grateful for the hospitality of the Shanghai Press Association today. This time, our Asahi aircraft departed from Tokyo and traveled safely all the way to Nanjing and Shanghai, creating a new record for flights between China and Japan, and can promote friendly relations between the two countries. We are very willing to continue to work hard to connect the feelings of the two countries. We will definitely report your country's hospitality to our country's citizens, hoping that the people of the two countries will maintain continuous friendship, and so on." Next, Mr. Kamio Shigeru, Director of the Eastern Department of the Asahi Shimbun, and Mr. Hada Hiroshi of the Shanghai Nichiho, successively gave speeches, both expressing that the Asahi aircraft's flight to China this time has created a record for the connection between the press circles of China and Japan, and hoping that China will also send aircraft to visit Japan in the near future. The Japanese press and all the people will definitely welcome it with the same enthusiasm. The guests chatted happily during the banquet, which did not end until about 10 PM.

Brought Letters The Asahi visiting aircraft came to Shanghai, bringing a letter from Mr. Ueno Seiichi, President of the Asahi Shimbun, to the Shanghai press, translated as follows: "To the gentlemen of the Shanghai Press Association: The two countries, China and Japan, which have always been friendly, have mistakenly entered a thorny path for more than a day. However, recently the situation has changed, and it has returned to the original relationship of mutual support between China and Japan. This is a very gratifying thing for the peace of China, Japan, and East Asia. This is all due to your excellent insight, the guidance of fair public opinion, and continued efforts. I would like to entrust our company's first Sino-Japanese civil aircraft, which is meaningful in connecting the capitals of Nanjing and Tokyo, to express my deep gratitude for the efforts of your colleagues and express my full respect. At the same time, I take this opportunity to wish you all good health and hope that you will make further efforts for the peace of East Asia and the friendship between China and Japan. Ueno Seiichi, President of the Osaka Tokyo Asahi Shimbun."

Today's Receptions This morning, Mr. Shinno and Mr. Tsukagoshi will go to the Municipal Government to visit Mayor Wu and Japanese Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi. At noon, the two gentlemen plan to host a banquet to entertain people from all walks of life in Shanghai. At 4 PM, Mayor Wu will host a tea party. At 7 PM, Japanese Ambassador Akira Ariyoshi will host a banquet. The two gentlemen are currently staying at the Banzai Hall and are scheduled to fly to Japan at 6 AM tomorrow morning.

Small Industrial and Commercial Credit Loans; Five Million Yuan Fully Raised; Chen Guangfu Separately Negotiates the Formation of a Banking Syndicate; Minister of Finance Kong Orders the Central Bank to Allocate Funds to Join; Measures Stipulated to Start Lending Next Week 116

According to the New Voice News Agency, the five million yuan for small industrial and commercial credit loans to help the market has now been fully raised. The banking syndicate is being formed immediately, and the money shops' expansion of loans has already been implemented. Details are as follows:

Formation of a Banking Syndicate

The subcommittee of the Bankers Association has resolved to form a banking syndicate to handle the five million yuan small industrial and commercial credit loan case. The issue of inviting member money shops of the Money Shops Association to join the cooperation has been negotiated by Chen Guangfu, Chairman of the Bankers Association, and Qin Runqing, Chairman of the Money Shops Association, and a request has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for an allocation of 2.5 million yuan to jointly form a banking syndicate for management. At the same time, Chen Guangfu, Chairman of the Bankers Association, had asked for instructions on the measures when he met with Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi the day before. Mr. Kong expressed his approval of the subcommittee's measures.

Fully Raised

The Bankers Association has already sent separate letters to its member banks, requesting them to report the number of small industrial and commercial credit loans they have identified within a time limit, so that they can be implemented as soon as possible. However, according to the New Voice News Agency reporter's investigation, the government's allocation of 2.5 million yuan has already been ordered by Minister Kong to be joined by the Central Bank to form a banking syndicate. As for the member banks of the Bankers Association, the subcommittee has also negotiated properly with the various banks and has identified 2 million yuan, of which 1 million yuan is from Bank of China, 500,000 yuan from Bank of Communications, and the remaining amount is identified by the member banks. If the money shops refuse to join, the identified banks will increase the amount proportionally to 2.5 million yuan.

Loans to Start Next Week

The member banks of the Bankers Association that have decided to join the banking syndicate, such as Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Shanghai Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Continental Bank, Jin City Bank, Salt Industry Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, China Industrial Bank, Kenye Bank, Xiye Bank, Guohuo Bank, Tongshang Bank, Guohua Bank, and Siming Bank, have decided to jointly establish a small industrial and commercial credit loan banking syndicate with the Central Bank. The establishment of this banking syndicate will be within the next week, and will be affiliated to the Central Bank or Bank of China in the future. Loan measures have also been drafted.

Money Shops' Attitude

The New Voice News Agency reporter inquired from the money shops yesterday. The Money Shops Association resolved at a provisional meeting of member representatives on the 15th of this month to expand credit loans without adding a banking syndicate. Now, all 57 member money shops have accepted the persuasion of Chairman Tai Runqing and have implemented the expansion. Therefore, the Money Shops Association's resolution on the subcommittee's decision to require continued accession will be based on the previous resolution's measures. Furthermore, the resolution of the change of the general meeting cannot be made without holding another general meeting.

Page 11

Inspection Tour of the New Life Movement: A Record of the Final Day 117

Yesterday Evening at Six O'Clock, Departed Shanghai for Hangzhou; Mr. Xu Expressed his Impressions of the Inspection

According to the Kuomintang News Agency, the New Life Movement Association's inspection tour group, consisting of Xu Qingyu, Zhang Yuchong, Lin Xueyan, and Yu Zhongqi, continued their group inspections of the New Life Movement yesterday.
