Shenbao Wireless Weekly

Intermediate Frequency Test Oscillator 194

— Ming Huan

Regarding the application and manufacturing methods of test oscillators, this magazine has previously introduced them in great detail. However, what was described only involved the high-frequency range. This article intends to specifically describe various intermediate-frequency test oscillators. Although the principles are the same, there are many differences in construction, application, and especially frequency calibration methods, so it is necessary to explain them separately.

Superheterodyne receivers have good performance and complex structures. Because of their unique intermediate frequency stage, it is extremely difficult to match them. Many amateur enthusiasts are daunted by the idea of making their own superheterodyne receivers, and even if they try, the results are rarely satisfactory. The main reason is the lack of accurate test oscillators to calibrate the circuits of the intermediate frequency stage to match its predetermined intermediate frequency.

Commercially manufactured superheterodyne receivers are sold only after several precise calibrations, but afterwards, due to various influences, they lose their original resonant state, leading to various problems. For example, the volume is weak, or the stations in the first half of the dial are very loud, while the second half is very weak, or sometimes the stations in the middle section are very loud, while the two ends become weak. In addition, there are squealing noises, and the same station appears at more than two points on the dial, etc. Most of these obstacles are due to improper adjustment of the intermediate frequency stage. If you are testing a superheterodyne receiver, relying only on measuring voltage and resistance, then no matter how accurate your voltmeter is, you will never be able to find the cause of these problems. Therefore, repairing superheterodyne receivers without an accurate intermediate frequency test oscillator is simply helpless.

Intermediate frequency oscillators are not difficult to manufacture, but the calibration of the frequency is difficult. The frequency of broadcasting frequency oscillators can be calibrated using the signals of many broadcasting stations, and shortwave oscillators can also be calibrated by referring to the signals of various shortwave stations. Only within the intermediate frequency range, there is no ready-made signal available. Fortunately, there is a simple method that only requires an ordinary broadcasting receiver to solve this problem.

Now, let us first describe the construction of a simple intermediate frequency oscillator. The circuit is shown in the figure. The capacity of each component is marked in the figure. Any triode vacuum tube can be used. The tuning coil can be wound on a one-and-a-quarter-inch diameter plastic tube with No. 20 double-yarn-covered wire, with fourteen turns per layer, for a total of fourteen layers. The center tap can be tapped out at the 98th turn. The coupling coil can be wound on the outer layer of the tuning coil, about six turns is enough.

After the oscillator is made, the second step is to calibrate its frequency. First, connect the output terminals of the oscillator to the antenna and ground connection of the broadcast receiver. Rotate the tuning capacitor of the oscillator to the center position, and then slowly rotate the tuning capacitor of the receiver until a sharp squealing sound is produced in the speaker. At this time, it indicates that the receiver is in resonance with the harmonic of the oscillator. When searching for this resonant point, an alternating current voltage must first be applied to the plate of the oscillator to modulate it, or the receiver must first self-oscillate, otherwise, this resonant point cannot be found, especially the latter method is more accurate. Any receiver can easily oscillate by simply increasing the coupling density of the screen grid.

After the first harmonic resonant point is found, record the accurate frequency number of the receiver at this time. Continue to rotate the receiver capacitor until the sharp squealing sound reappears. This is the resonant point of adjacent harmonics. The frequency difference between the two resonant points of the receiver is the basic frequency of the oscillator. For example, if you want the frequency of the oscillator to be 175KC, you must gradually change its tuning capacitor to make the frequency difference between the two resonant points of the receiver exactly 175KC.

Various Wiring Methods for Low-Frequency Transformers 195

— Qing Shi

If a medium-sized transformer is used properly, good results can usually be obtained. There are many ways to connect it. As long as you know the effects of various uses, you can choose the most suitable one. In this short article, I will write down the main connection methods of low-frequency transformers, so that general amateurs can test them one by one and choose them at will, without groping in the dark.

In the first type of experiment, the best transformation ratio of the transformer to be used can be determined. Various transformers (except for a one-to-one ratio) can obtain four different ratios. The first figure shows the usual connection method of a transformer. The plate of the previous vacuum tube is connected to P of the primary winding, and B is directly or through a bleeder resistor to the positive pole of the battery. The grid of the next tube should be connected to G of the secondary winding, and F should be connected to the negative pole of the C battery.

We can also assemble the transformer into an autotransformer. This only requires connecting B of the primary winding and F of the secondary winding. In this connection, the entire coil is combined to make the secondary winding, while the primary winding uses the original primary winding (Figure 2) or the original secondary winding (Figure 3).

For example, if we have a one-to-two transformer, then in Figure 1-1, we can transform it into a one-to-three. In Figure 3, the ratio is two to three, in other words, one to one point five.

Finally, we can also use the autotransformer as a one-to-one temporarily. This only requires connecting it as shown in Figure 4. The name of this type of connection is impedance-capacity-resistance.

In Figures 2, 3, and 4, the capacity of the capacitor method is about 0.005 to 0.05 microfarads, and the leakage resistor R is about 200,000 to 1 million ohms. (It must be determined by experiment)

Now, we must also pay attention that if the current of the previous vacuum tube exceeds three milliamperes, the core of the transformer will be saturated, causing audio distortion. Therefore, a more suitable method is to separate the alternating current component of the plate current from its direct current component, and only let the former pass through the winding of the transformer.

The device in Figure 5 can help us achieve this isolation. The direct current passes through the resistor R (which can be selected between 30,000 and 100,000 ohms), while the alternating current easily passes through the coupling capacitor C. This will not cause saturation.

The quantity of the resistor R is related to the internal resistance of the previous vacuum tube and the maximum voltage used on its plate. Therefore, it is best to decide after experimenting.

In addition, Figures 5, 6, 7, and 8 are related to Figures 1, 2, 3, and 4. As for the experimental comparison method, it is best not to use radio, but to use a pickup, always using the same record and a new needle.

Trivial Notes on Lead-Aluminum Rectification 196

— Liang Yingchang

(1) Of the chemicals used in lead-aluminum rectification, sodium bicarbonate and borax are more common. Sodium bicarbonate dissolves to give a more concentrated solution, which performs better than borax.

(2) Ordinary regulations require the use of distilled water, which may be due to the common use of distilled water in chemical laboratories, because it does not contain impurities and is reliable to use. In fact, ordinary purified water can also work equally well.

(3) The lead and aluminum sheets must be at least one inch above the water surface, otherwise the copper screws connecting the wires will easily be stained with the solution during operation. After the copper screws are stained with the solution, they will undergo a chemical reaction, which can prevent the passage of current, thus reducing performance or causing work to stop.

(4) The voltage after rectification is still unstable, and its voltage count cannot be measured without adding other equipment. However, the current after rectification has become unidirectional, which can be measured with an ammeter.

(5) Full-wave rectification is not easy to use, because the internal resistance of each bottle (full-wave rectification must use at least two rectifier bottles) should be equal; otherwise, the power output by each bottle will be very different. To maximize the effectiveness of full-wave rectification, the size, distance, and thickness of the solution of each bottle of lead and aluminum should be completely the same.

(6) The biggest drawback of lead-aluminum rectifiers is that they are prone to heat generation and rapid corrosion of the aluminum sheet. The only way to avoid this is to increase the area of lead and aluminum and increase the solution, while reducing the charging rate. Approximately one liter of solution per bottle, one hundred square inches of lead and aluminum, passing one ampere of current, can last for a long time without heating up.

(7) In order to prevent the evaporation of the solution, a certain book teaches people to add a layer of oil on top of the solution, which is not a good method, because the first thing to prevent when using this rectifier is to prevent it from heating up, and the evaporation of the solution is to release its own power. After adding oil, the heating of the solution is accelerated instead.

(8) Shan Tong stipulates that each rectifier bottle can withstand a voltage of 50 volts. To use it at 100 volts, two bottles must be connected in series. In fact, if the current passing through is properly limited to prevent the rectifier from getting too hot, it is also possible to use only one bottle at 100 volts without damage.

(9) When using lead-aluminum rectification, whether using a transformer or directly connecting to an AC power source, it is necessary to prevent discharge after the power source is cut off. Therefore, where there is no generator, charging should be stopped immediately before the power plant cuts off the power.

(10) After the rectifier has been working, the white substance accumulated on the lead and aluminum should be removed immediately to avoid reducing working efficiency. After use, the solution can be poured off, the precipitate removed, and the clean solution saved. A small amount of sodium bicarbonate can be added next time to continue using it, but it should not be stored for too long.

Another Device for Testing Lead-Acid Batteries 197

— Wang Maosheng

The common instruments for testing lead-acid batteries are a hydrometer or a voltmeter. Now there is also a cadmium tester, which can not only measure the number of voltages, but also check the state of discharge and charge of the positive and negative plates. Its structure, as shown in the first figure, is a combination of a voltmeter, two copper rods, and a cadmium strip. The graduation of the voltmeter is shown in the second figure.

During testing, the cadmium strip is inserted into sulfuric acid, but it must not come into contact with the positive and negative plates, and left for a moment. When testing the positive plate, the other copper rod should be connected to the positive terminal. When testing the negative plate, the other copper rod should be touched to the negative terminal. After the cadmium strip is inserted into sulfuric acid, it will initiate a local chemical reaction, generating voltage. The magnitude of this voltage can show whether the two plates are good or bad. The values are as follows:

(1) Charging: Positive pole 2.3v－2.45v (less than this number, the positive plate is sick)

Negative pole (0.iv) — (0.2v) (close to 〇 or above 〇, the negative plate is sick)

(2) Discharging: Positive pole approximately 2.05v Negative pole 0.25v Less than the ratio value, the plate is sick, and must be charged. The above values are shown on the second voltmeter.

Neg Discharged refers to the negative pole during discharge, Charged refers to the negative pole during charging Pos Discharged refers to the positive pole during discharge, Charged refers to the positive pole during charging

As for the voltage calculation of the battery, an example can be used to illustrate it.

Charging: Voltage between cadmium and negative pole is —0.1

Voltage between cadmium and positive pole is 十2.45

Voltage of battery＝2.45＋0.1＝2.45v

Discharging: Voltage between cadmium and negative pole is 0.25

Voltage between cadmium and positive pole is 2.05

Voltage of battery＝2.05—0.25＝1.81v

Small Experiences 198

— Qi

(1) Economical Metal Chassis

Metal chassis for radios are both beautiful and convenient. Especially for AC radios, it can eliminate annoying AC noise. However, if aluminum plates are used for this metal chassis, the price is quite expensive, which is not in line with the economic conditions of general amateurs. I would like to contribute an alternative for comrades to try.

First find a biscuit box of suitable size made of tinplate (if there are other suitable tinplate boxes, they can also be used). Wash off the trademarks and patterned paper attached to the surface, or wipe it clean with sandpaper. Then mix aluminum powder (Al luminrim Powder) (commonly known as aluminum powder, sold in various paint stores) with thin glue and apply it evenly to make it smooth and beautiful. After it is dry, it becomes a practical metal chassis.

(2) Ingenious Pointer

The pointer on the dial is usually a line engraved on the panel, or a pointed indicator cut from paper is used to indicate it. The former damages the panel, which is not very appropriate. The latter is even more simple and crude, and once it is soiled, there is the trouble of replacing it from time to time. Here is a method, using only an ordinary drawing pin, and pressing it on the edge of the dial. The pointed hole in the center of the thumbtack, with the reflection of the panel, has become a natural indicator. (A is the thumbtack, B is the dial.)

Experiences in Assembling a 6F7 Single-Tube Radio 199

— Yang Xuelun

The goal of amateur researchers is nothing more than to hope to assemble a radio that is inexpensive and highly efficient. However, if the cost is low, the efficiency will certainly not be high; if the efficiency is high, the cost will certainly not be low. Since the advent of composite vacuum tubes, this problem has been considerably solved. Because one composite vacuum tube can perform the work of two or more tubes, its efficiency is indeed superior to that of ordinary vacuum tubes. I previously read the "Economic Exchange of 6F7 Dual-Tube Radio" by Mr. Yongyan and Mr. Wu Yingjian in the Shen Bao Wireless Radio Weekly. I immediately purchased one, assembled it according to the diagram, and received nearby radio stations. The volume was indeed loud, comparable to that of an ordinary three-tube radio. However, I could not receive any of the major Shanghai radio stations, even with headphones. It was either too regenerative and howling, or there was a "poof" sound and silence. After repeated disassembly and assembly, I finally discovered the source of the problem. As Mr. Zhang Shouyu stated, the screen grid voltage should not be higher than the detector plate voltage. I will now describe the modified circuit diagram and reception situation in detail as follows:

L 35 mm inner diameter spiderweb coil, 14 turns of No. 26 enameled wire

L1 Same as above, 65 turns

L2 Same as above, 35 turns

C .00046 microfarad variable capacitor

C1 .00025 microfarad fixed capacitor

C2 1 microfarad fixed capacitor

C3 .0005 microfarad fixed capacitor

R2 2 megohm grid leak

R1 500 ohm wire-wound resistor

R2 100,000 ohm potentiometer

R3 75 ohm wire-wound center-tapped resistor

R4 25,000 ohm carbon resistor

RFC Radio high-frequency choke coil (using high-quality domestic goods)

T 3r/2:1 transformer (using high-quality domestic goods) LS loudspeaker

The distance between the two spiderweb coils L and L1 is 5 mm, and the distance between the two spiderweb coils L1 and L2 is 10 mm. The three spiderweb coils are fixed with screws and do not need to be moved. Regeneration is controlled by a potentiometer, so it is extremely stable. When this radio receives Shanghai in Changzhou, the potentiometer can only be turned halfway. The five radio stations, China West, Shanghai, Dongfang, Li Shutang, and Fuxing, can all play sound through the loudspeaker. As for receiving the Central Radio Station and the various radio stations in Changzhou and Wuxi, the impedance value of the potentiometer can be reduced according to the desired volume.

The power supply can be either AC or DC. If using DC, a 6V storage battery can be used, or four cylindrical dry batteries can be connected in series. If it is a semi-AC type, a doorbell transformer can be rewound to supply it. The B voltage must be up to 135V.

Finance: Market Sentiment Continues to Rise, Gold Market Recovers by $4.43 200

The Reasons for American Cotton's Instability 207

Weak Demand…Floating Profits Being Taken…Increased Selling

Turbulent Times…New Cotton Policies…Still Undecided

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened higher due to favorable overseas news. Dealers, mainland merchants, and Liverpool buyers bought in, and prices rose by three to four points in all months. Subsequently, demand weakened, scattered long positions were closed, and local and New Orleans sellers entered the market, causing the market to turn weaker. Simultaneously, this prompted brokers to increase selling and close positions at any cost. Furthermore, the instability of the European situation and the indecisiveness of the U.S. regarding new cotton policies also caused anxiety. Ultimately, short covering and repeat purchases by dealers caused prices to rebound, and the market closed firm. Spot prices rose by five points, while futures prices fell by two to six points. The British cotton market was strong, with spot prices rising by ten points and futures prices rising by one to five points. The Indian cotton market was firm and rising, with Pingguoer rising by 4.5 rupees, Aomula rising by 7.5 rupees, and Bairoxi rising by 6.5 rupees. Grain and Flour: The Forward Market Weakens Again 208

Yesterday's flour market saw relatively stable prices in all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat was quoted at about 12 cents higher in Chicago and 8 cents higher in Canada. When prices opened, foreign wheat was quoted higher, and the current month was tight due to limited spot flour supply, stabilizing sentiment. Although the weather had cleared, trading in all months was still active, but the weakness in the rice market inevitably brought some weakness to the flour market, with prices only improving by 2.5 to 5 percent compared to the previous day. When the afternoon session opened, prices were initially stable, but then gradually declined again. This was due to the absence of outside investors and market rumors of factories continuing to order a shipment of Australian wheat at a price of 4.77 yuan, causing sentiment to weaken. In the current situation, the near-term is firm while the distant-term is weak. As a result, the current month fell by 5 percent, April fell by 1.25 cents, May fell by 1.5 cents, June fell by 1 cent, July fell by 1.25 cents, and August fell by 5 percent.

More Active Buying in Distant-Term Wheat 209

Yesterday's forward wheat market saw relatively stable prices in all months after the morning opening. Foreign wheat was quoted at 8 to 12 cents higher. Trading in the current month was naturally slow due to the proximity of the delivery date. However, sentiment was relatively weak due to the influx of foreign wheat. Distant-term months saw more active buying due to the scarcity of hedging. Opening prices in all months were 12 cents higher. When the afternoon session opened, the current month's market remained weak, closing at only 3.50 yuan. This was due to the stockpiling of foreign wheat, leaving bulls with little room to maneuver. Mainland traders entered the distant-term months, stabilizing the market. As a result, July and August were both up by 2 cents, while other months saw no price change. The spot wheat market was stable, with Shandong Su wheat opening at 3.64 yuan, Mingguang wheat at 3.65 yuan, and Hankou wheat at 3.34 yuan. Fuxin sold 2,000 bags, and Xinda sold 1,500 bags.

Japonica and Indica Rice Both Flat and Weak 210

Yesterday, shipments of japonica rice to South Shanghai suddenly increased again, totaling 36 or 37 boats (over 7,000 shi of cargo). Sales were only slightly active in the local area, with sales of packaged rice being sluggish. Only the Yantai group purchased a few hundred bags, so the overall market was stable with a hint of weakness. Prices for both thick japonica and thin indica rice remained stable, with no significant changes. Du Yangjian rice was not traded, and the supply of Yin Yuan exceeded demand, causing prices to fall sharply by 12 cents. Only Bian Yuan rice has been out of stock for a long time, and once it is available, it will be stable. The North Shanghai rice market saw a surge in supply from various rivers after the Yujidun river channel reopened the night before, with about 70 or 80 boats arriving. Sales of various types of rice were weak, with mid-grade white japonica falling by 1 cent, early thin indica falling by 7 or 8 cents, and Du Jian falling by 5 or 6 cents. Sheep-tip rice was scarce, and prices were firm. Other prices remained unchanged.

The foreign rice market was initially weak, but sales improved due to strong demand from tea merchants and the mainland, especially poor areas and Chongsha. A total of 13,000 to 14,000 bags were sold throughout the day, causing the market to turn from weak to stable. The native indica market has been suppressed by foreign rice for a long time. Yesterday, cargo owners dumped goods to sell, resulting in prices falling by 1 cent. Local, mainland, and Chongsha buyers then purchased over 2,000 bags.

Sugar Market: Rumor of Increased Tax on Foreign Sugar, Guangdong Coarse Sugar White Rises by 3 Dimes 213

Yesterday's sugar market saw great excitement due to widespread rumors that the increased tax on foreign sugar would be implemented on April 1st. As a result, there were no asking prices for goods such as 24 coarse sugar white. The long-sluggish market showed signs of an immediate price surge. At 2:30 PM, the Sugar Industry Cooperative Company auctioned off three batches of Guangdong coarse sugar white: (1) 1,608 bags of high-quality goods, with a reserve price of 17 yuan; (2) 1,300 bags of slightly lower-quality goods, with a reserve price of 16.9 yuan; (3) 1,010 bags of lower-quality goods, with a reserve price of 16.8 yuan. Over 40 companies attended the auction, and most submitted bids for the entire lot. As a result, those bidding for the entire lot only received 97 bags. The entire lot was sold cleanly, creating a temporary frenzy. It is rumored that the reserve price will be increased again at next Monday's auction. Yesterday, prices rose by 2.5 to 3 dimes. The association set a post-auction price of 17 yuan for 24 coarse sugar white, but no sale was made. Transshipment goods were sold at 4.9 yuan, an increase of 1 dime and 8 cents. Chaoqing sugar also showed signs of tightening. Goods from brands were scarce.

Silk and Tea: Chinese Silk in Desperate Export Situation 215

The export of silk is becoming increasingly dismal. There is almost no news from European and American customers. Based on current Citibank prices, the overseas price of Chinese silk is only around 350 yuan. However, Japanese silk is still able to compete in the world market at this low price. According to Reuters market reports, Japanese silk sales in the US are still over 2,000 bales per day (including both spot and futures). The Indian yellow and white coarse silk market is also dominated by Japanese factory silk. Furthermore, the domestic sales of Chinese silk are also being impacted by rayon. It is truly heartbreaking to see this.

According to a silk industry tycoon, the management of factories in China regarding weaving and reeling, as well as the discounts on silk cocoons, urgently needs to be improved in order to support the struggling industry. In recent years, the financial community has long shied away from investing in the silk industry. The only hope is for effective government relief and a new situation after the unified control of silk cocoons. Currently, only Baotai Silk Factory is operating in Shanghai. The future of the silk industry is bleak, so it is hoped that the authorities and members of society will pay close attention.

Increased Tea Tax in French Colonies Confirmed 216

It has been confirmed that the French colonies in Africa have increased tea taxes. The Alen region of Africa, a part of the French colonies, imports no less than 40,000 boxes of Chinese green tea annually. Historically, this region collected an import tax of 400 francs per 100 kilograms of Chinese tea. Last summer, the Alen colonial government resolved to double the tax. Subsequently, our government repeatedly protested to the French government based on the principle of reciprocity, and the matter remained unresolved for a long time. Sources from within the tea industry have now confirmed that the increased tea tax has been implemented. However, due to China's opposition, the tax rate was only increased by one-third of the original rate, that is, 600 francs per 100 kilograms, equivalent to 120 yuan in Chinese silver per 100 kilograms. Based on this situation, the sales of high-quality Zhenmei tea from China will be significantly impacted.

Cotton-like Silk Rayon Pongee, Exclusively Domestic Product 217

Plain, Slanting Flower Rayon Pongee Imported from Overseas

Rayon pongee comes in three types: slanting flower, plain, and silk-like, all used for lining suits. Silk-like rayon pongee is entirely a domestic product. Plain and slanting flower are all foreign products. Slanting flower is more expensive and has fewer users. Plain and silk-like are slightly more popular. Since domestic silk-like rayon pongee is inexpensive and beautiful, and Western-style clothing stores in Shanghai and other cities are using it as much as possible, the import volume of rayon pongee has decreased year by year. Yesterday, the top-grade silk-like rayon pongee from Guohuo Daohua sold wholesale for 6 dimes and 7.5 cents per yard. Hengfeng Xinhua No. 2 goods sold for 5 dimes and 4 cents. Miscellaneous No. 3 goods sold for 4 dimes and 7 or 8 cents. Imported slanting flower rayon pongee sold for 2.2 yuan, top-grade plain sold for 1.8 yuan, and No. 2 sold for 1.7 yuan. Deji's Riri Deli Jinshan rayon pongee sold for 9 dimes and 5 cents.

Free Talk

Naoya Shiga's Everyday Life Novels 218

— Zhang Xiangshan

From the 40th year of the Meiji period onwards, the Japanese literary scene can be said to have been dominated by Naturalism. After the 43rd year, the emergence of the magazine "Shirakaba" further ignited the great storm of Naturalism. At that time, the basic members of the "Shirakaba" group were Saneatsu Mushanokōji and Naoya Shiga, and Shiga Naoya's art became generally recognized at the same time as the "Shirakaba" magazine swept the literary scene.

If readers are not forgetful, they will remember the "New Village Movement" that caused a sensation for a time! The magazine "Shirakaba" was the vehicle for this movement. Although the movement itself only survives in name, Naoya Shiga, who gained the most popularity in short stories and was a basic member of this movement, is now living a quiet old age in Abiko and has practically withdrawn from his literary career.

Because the author's life is ordinary, he is particularly faithful to real life. He does not have the courage of Zola and others to go to jail or hotels to experience the taste of ordinary people's lives. Therefore, the ordinary life surrounding the author himself has often become a never-ending source of creative material. Works created with this kind of material can be called everyday life novels. Everyday life novels have no grand illusions, and even less "creation from nothing." They express an author's personality and life in an extremely natural way.

Naoya Shiga's novels are mostly short stories. There is probably only one long novel, "A Dark Night's Passing." In his short stories, it can be said that seven or eight out of ten are everyday life novels, the author's own life. I have read seven or eight out of ten of his novels. If I were not an Easterner, possessing Eastern upbringing, it would indeed be difficult to finish even one of his works due to the ordinariness and simplicity of Naoya Shiga's novels.

Even the non-everyday life novels still cannot escape his ordinary choices. So-called shallow righteous figures, students, and deformed people are often realistically presented by him, such as "Van's Crime," "Qingbing's Sanitary Gourd," and "The Student's God." These people are either trembling for survival, or clinging to petty righteousness without speaking their names, or have deformed hobbies, or seek justice on the road. They are truly so-called petty righteous commoners, all realistically portrayed. These characters are all essentially Easterners, especially suited to the lives of ordinary townspeople before and after the Meiji Restoration. Moreover, they are men from Kanto (the old name for Tokyo), not like the characters from Kansai portrayed by Jun'ichirō Tanizaki. Simply put, they are "Edo (the old name for Tokyo) men." They are the products of the commoner thought and chivalrous spirit of the Tokugawa era.

As for Naoya Shiga's everyday life novels, they are roughly divided into four types: personal trivialities, muddled travels, hobbies, and simple, winding relationships with women. Personal trivialities refer to personal matters such as his own likeness and family affairs. Here, he treats sweeping his child's grave, his hatred for his father, the death of his mother and the story of marrying a new mother, his dislike for his grandmother on his grandfather's anniversary, and even the search for a lost dog as subjects for his novels, such as "Reconciliation," "Kensaku's Reminiscences," "Mother's Death and a New Mother," "One Morning," and "Ink Dog." These stories are mostly childhood memories. Although they are too bland, they have a naive and innocent interest because they are expressions of childhood psychology and phenomena. The second type is muddled travels. Muddled travels means running around without a clear purpose, often going from Kanto to Kansai, from Nara to Kōbe, with a nervous disposition. He also sometimes looks for a house in Kyoto all day long but cannot find one, and is even so hungry that he cannot lift his feet but refuses to buy food outside, fearing that he will be infected with all kinds of epidemics. He is truly muddled, as if traveling in a dream, such as in "Living Elsewhere," "Kugenuma Trip," "Okitsu," "Returning to the Capital," "Trivial Matters," and "Condolences for the Earthquake." As for the third type of hobby, it is his internal observation of his life, such as viewing paintings and watching plays. He likes to appreciate ancient paintings, so Buddhist temples often become his places of appreciation. Whether in rainy or windy weather, he can make an appointment with friends to visit Buddhist temples to see ancient paintings. This elegant behavior still retains the elegance of literati in the feudal era, such as in "Toriwo's Illness" and "Twenties." The fourth type, love affairs with women, fully exposes the author's ordinariness. In these love affairs, the male protagonist is a man who is afraid of his wife, but still does some romantic things outside. Sometimes he is even extremely cowardly, fearing his wife's suspicion of him. He sees signs that his maid is pregnant, and thinks that the maid has had an affair, but he is afraid that his wife will suspect him, so he is uneasy day and night. Finally, he confesses to his wife. This kind of timid protagonist makes the reader feel extremely impatient. He even makes the male protagonist feel the pain of a dual personality of love because of the woman's helpless suffering. Examples of these works include "Good People's Marriage," "Infatuation," "Trivial Matters," and "Late Autumn."

In short, when we look at the above four types, we can clearly understand Naoya Shiga's personality: he is a timid, feudal, and suspicious person. Therefore, the stories surrounding his body are also extremely trivial, timid, and suspicious stories.

Someone once criticized Naoya Shiga, saying, "He has too stable a life. If his life were that of a worker or a farmer, then his works would be much more worthwhile." I somewhat agree with this opinion. With his direct and naturalistic skills, he could perfectly describe the hardships of ordinary people's lives, but unfortunately, the life surrounding him is so ordinary.

Naoya Shiga does not regard literature as a profession, and even despises those who regard literature as a profession. Therefore, he is not very passionate about creation, but only regards literature as the same attitude that ancient literati had towards poetry.

Since the end of 1933, after publishing the same "Afternoon on a Sunday," he has completely retreated into seclusion like a cicada in autumn. However, his ordinary and simple naturalistic approach is considered to need review, and the everyday life novels of the Naoya Shiga era are still constantly being produced in the modern literary scene. This is indeed a sad thing.

Hope 219

— Wei Zhongtian

Hope is like an endless desert, like an unclimbable mountain. People are forever climbing this mountain, climbing! Those who climb well, climb up segment by segment, those who don't, fall to the foot of the mountain. Those with courage can continue to climb, otherwise, they will forever hide in the trap of despair and sigh.

Humanity, whoever they may be, all have this notion of "hope". Even the most foolish and stupid person has their own hopes, only differing in size. Humanity has never had satisfied desires. When one hope is achieved, another thing is hoped for. Because of this, humanity is often dragged into the abyss of depression by "hope". In the past, many people ridiculed Emperor Qin Shi Huang for wanting to become an immortal after becoming emperor, wanting to make himself immortal. They ridiculed him for being too insatiable, but who isn't like that? Having fame, one still wants money. Having money, one still wants a beautiful concubine. Having a concubine, one still wants... This desire will never be satisfied, unless one is lying in a coffin.

At the same time, before each hope is realized, the heart always holds infinite enthusiasm and longing. However, when that hope is in hand, it feels bland and ordinary! People are forever unable to escape boredom and pain in this situation!

Let me take myself as an example. When I was a child, I saw my older brothers and uncles always with pockets full of money, and with many new clothes to wear, and could hit children at will. I was really envious, thinking that it would be great if I were a young man. However, when I grew up, I didn't feel that it was so great, instead, I missed my childhood life. For another example, when I was in middle school, I saw others going to Shanghai to study at university, wearing suits and shiny leather shoes, and I was very envious! Later, I was fortunate enough to go to Shanghai to attend university, but I didn't feel any joy. At this time, I saw others going abroad to study, and I was also dreaming, thinking that if I had the opportunity to study abroad in the future, that would be truly being a "darling of fortune". However, now I am really living a mediocre life in a foreign country, and my current life is still so lonely and so dull! Therefore, I say that people's energy is completely exhausted in the process of hoping, stopping only when their eyes are closed.

I have seen many friends, when he or she is living a single life, truly hoping every day, even dreaming, hoping that he or she would have a lover to accompany him or her through life, that would be happiness; but when he or she one day really finds a lover, isn't he or she still knitting his or her brows, staring at the gray sky and sighing, feeling bored! At this time, they will feel that love is "nothing more than that"!

When every hope is realized, disappointment follows.

Like recently, I always hoped to buy an exquisite vase to put on the bookshelf, and insert a bunch of bright flowers, lilacs or daffodils, so that I could smell the fragrance of lilacs when I came back after class. I believed that a lot of warmth would be transmitted from the fragrance of lilacs to my soul. At this time, I might feel infinite joy! But now, I bought the vase almost ten days ago, and I have already changed several bunches of bright flowers. Dandelions, lilacs, and purple cloud beans have all been inserted, but they don't seem to make me love them in any way. On the contrary, every time I see a piece or two of withered flowers falling on the bookshelf, it makes me symbolize my future life even more.

Man and Wild Boar 220

— Hei Ying

"Wild boars, they are truly frightening wild creatures!" The storyteller ended his lengthy and tedious narrative with this sentence. Crystal-like beads of sweat seeped from the wrinkles on his forehead, but he didn't bother to wipe them away, only shaking his large head, muttering to himself, indicating that he still found it terrifying to think about. But I walked away nonchalantly, cursing in my heart:

"Cowardly thing!"

But dear readers: here I should tell you that I also encountered wild boars half a year after hearing that story. It was nighttime, and I had no defense at all, so I almost lost my life.

It happened when I was an apprentice at a small port. My father sent me to this tailor shop like a piece of merchandise, and I was handed over to the boss: "Boss, this child is in your hands, please take care of him and teach him." After saying that, he took the original train back. According to the rules here, apprentices are not paid wages, and can only exchange more than ten hours of labor a day for a meal and the worst place to sleep. In the morning, before anyone else got up, I had to leave the warm dreamland and quietly go downstairs to boil water for tea, wash cups, and sweep the floor. Around seven o'clock, when the shop opened and the clerks had all arrived, I had to hurry up and burn the charcoal for the iron, otherwise the boss would twist my ear and scold me. So I had to go to the boss's wife, "What vegetables should I buy today?" Standing in front of this woman with a pockmarked face but a kind heart, I waited like a wooden statue for her instructions. She touched the dense spots on her face, thought for a moment, and as usual handed me the shopping basket, telling me what vegetables to buy back. In this way, I had to go to the vegetable market at least once a day.

Once I saw a wild boar in the vegetable market, hanging bloody, its protruding eyeballs frighteningly large. A group of children surrounded it, gesticulating and telling stories about hunting wild boars—saying that the wild boar hunters set off last night, a total of five people, carrying shotguns, walking to the back of the rubber plantation about twenty miles from the market, and as a result, when they came back this morning, they brought this one back.

The wild boar hunters were resting in the coffee shop. I passed by there, stopped and listened for a while: "...The danger is also quite...You know, when they charged up in a large group, we were hiding in the trees firing guns..."

That day, the entire small port was shaken by a wild boar. Children were shouting and jumping; adults were talking. I recalled the person who told the wild boar story last time, and thought to myself, "If I also had the opportunity to hunt wild boars!"

The opportunity finally came. But it was extremely accidental. One of the shop's collection clerks became ill. At this time, the clothes bill of a Dutch foreman in a nearby rubber plantation was due, and the boss was anxious to collect it. He looked for a long time and couldn't find a way, and finally grabbed me to the counter and said: "The appointment with the Dutchman must not be missed; do you know, he is waiting for you to collect it. If you don't go today, he will definitely not give it to you! They are like that! Go there, okay?" He put on a pleading expression, "It's not far, you can get there in two hours by bicycle."

I had to listen to the boss. Moreover, the boss and the collection clerk always used that bicycle, and I had never enjoyed it. Wouldn't I be able to ride it happily for half a day to the plantation this time? In this way, around two o'clock in the afternoon, I took the bill the boss gave me and set off on the bicycle.

There weren't many people on the road, and both sides were wilderness. The sun shone fiercely on my head. Occasionally, a truck loaded with coconut shells drove past with a rumble, stirring up a cloud of yellow mud and sand, almost making me unable to see the road. The road gradually became uneven, with several places suddenly rising high, as if they were a hill; but when you climbed up with effort, it took no effort to go down again. Then came another hill, and then down again...

When I arrived at the S plantation, I was already exhausted, probably around four o'clock at this time. I asked: "Is the foreman Yokman in?" The answer was that he had gone to the plantation and couldn't come out until five o'clock; there was no way, I had to sit outside the door of that wooden house.

Everything was quiet, without sound, except for the old man pushing a cart, clipping the grass in front of the door with a "cha-cha" sound, I couldn't see any other living thing.

Here I thought, if I get the bill at five o'clock, and then spend two hours on the road back to the shop, won't it be dark? That would be a little awkward. What if I encountered something on the road—like a wild boar, how should I, with no experience, avoid it? After thinking that way, I began to feel uneasy.

Sure enough, on the way back to the shop after receiving the not-so-large amount of money, pushing hard on the bicycle pedals, the sky had changed from gray to black. I lit the small oil lamp in front of the car and groped forward on the yellow sand road. My heart was pounding all the way. At the same time, I was also cursing the boss in my heart: "No conscience! Clearly knowing that I wouldn't be able to make it back today, he still forced me to go; now—" Suddenly a nerve-wracking scream came from the wilderness on the left, and the opposite wilderness seemed to shrink away, a piece of water stretching out. Then I heard a burst of heavy footsteps rushing forward, and the cries of a pig that seemed to have gone mad. My whole body was shaking, I couldn't go forward on either side, and in a panic, I jumped off the car. Immediately, the fierce beast had already approached my side, and I had no choice but to jump into the pool of water. Fortunately, the depth of the water only reached my thighs; standing there watching a thing that was twice as big as the wild boar hanging in the vegetable market pass by, my heart suffocated as if it had been hit by a stone, and then it recovered, and I found the bicycle and fled back.

The next day, I resigned from my apprentice position at the tailor shop. Because of the boss's kindness, he gave me two dollars to buy a third-class train ticket home. When I saw my father, I told him about the experience of almost being eaten by a wild boar; but he unexpectedly said to me: "Child, let me tell you: to live, you must risk life and death; do you think there will be no danger without wild boars? You are wrong. People sometimes eat people too!"

So, on the third day, I was sent back to that tailor shop again.

War Miscellany (9) 221

— By Tokunaga Nao, translated by Ye Yin

Rice that couldn't fit in the warehouse was piled in front of the store.

But the rice in the warehouse wasn't being evacuated anywhere.

My father, who wasn't a permanent employee, simply didn't have work to do for ten or twenty days.

My mother, who went to get "leftovers," fought with my father every day.

"When Dad comes back, he'll definitely become rich; then, we won't be called 'leftover eaters' anymore, and life will get better..."—My hope completely fell flat.

When I was a second-grader, my older sister was already a fourth-grader. Because my sister was a girl, she was able to pay more detailed attention to the family's living situation than me; she discussed it with my mother herself, dropped out of school, and became a worker at the tobacco monopoly bureau.

Falsely claiming her unqualified age of thirteen as fifteen, in order to get a daily wage of sixteen cents, my sister got up at five in the morning and hurriedly ran to the monopoly bureau a mile away from home.

My sister was small in age, but very mature; however, her height was as small as mine. My sister, with a dirty towel holding a lunch box tucked under her arm, ran home in the evening, very hurried. In order to have a sixteen-cent salary to collect, my sister was really hurried.

"Because compulsory education has been extended to six years, you must go to school." Although there was also urging from the village chief and the principal; however, my mother ignored it. My sister simply didn't care either.

(IV)

The following year, I entered the third grade, placing third in the exam. Among the students in elementary school, there was also mutual discussion about teachers accepting bribes from children's guardians to deliberately inflate or deflate the released grades.

However, I didn't care about that kind of thing at all. There were also classmates who provoked me, saying that the class leader Ueno's academic ability was not as good as mine, and asked me what I thought; but for me, that kind of thing was fine no matter what. Anyway, I wouldn't be able to enter middle school, and after graduating from the fourth grade, I would have to rush to work in some factory to earn money—for me, who was thinking that way, that kind of thing was completely unwilling to get involved in.

That year, my mother gave birth to another baby. There were already five of us siblings. In order to take care of the newborn boy, the days I didn't go to school were even more than before. Often, I wouldn't go to class for a whole week.

Even so, I wasn't unhappy to go to school. I liked carrying my youngest brother on my back, standing near the back door, looking at various books. Whether it was the Chinese textbook, the illustrated novels, or old women's magazines, I often read them using only the method of looking at the letters. And I was very good at reading Chinese characters with Han sounds. The novels, etc., were marked with several kinds of pronunciations, and when the people nearby came to listen, I would proudly read out Iwami Jūtarō's slaying of the big snake, Hachi-ryū den, Kan'ei San-bajutsu, etc.

Transfer Transport 222

— Huang Feng

The school holds the machine wheel,

Eyes fixed ahead,

Letting the two tracks

Unfold before you—

Holding on tight,

Transporting;

Flowing through plains,

Winding through mountains;

Not letting negligence climb into the heart,

Not letting fatigue stick to the body;

Obeying orders

Is that rapidly turning iron wheel,

For it, the

Song of life is composed;

The song,

Startles the heavens,

Shakes the earth,

All around is filled with

The echo of progress!

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

The Problem of Incorrect Characters 223

— Ba Shan

In recent years, the issue of incorrect characters has been a hot topic in literary circles.

First, there was Mr. Liu Bannong's doggerel, mocking the "advocating" and "studying abroad" of exam candidates; then there was Mr. Cao Juren's advocacy of incorrect characters, and Mr. Lu Xun's sophistry on the application of incorrect characters. This has already attracted a lot of attention. Recently, "common characters" are being promoted collectively, and the advocacy of incorrect characters is intentional. This has become a major issue in writing and using characters.

Originally, ancient people used incorrect characters, which is the so-called method of "general borrowing". The "false borrowing" category in the Six Writings of the Han people is also an explanation of the application of incorrect characters. And because of the differences in dialects in various places, people now are still actually using incorrect characters. The local phrase "man hao" (quite good) is called "man hao" (full good) in some places; therefore, some people write "man hao" in literary books, and some people write "man hao," but in fact "man" (蠻) and "man" (滿) are both correct, and are not incorrect characters; but for people in places that speak the dialect of "man hao," the phrase "man hao" is seen as an incorrect character. In order to eradicate illiteracy and facilitate literacy, it is correct to teach people to read in various places using local dialects, even if it means using incorrect characters. Because even though they are incorrect characters, it is much easier for illiterate people to understand them by recognizing the sound. However, although I agree with the application of incorrect characters, it is only as mentioned above, when teaching illiterate people to read that the application of incorrect characters is correct; but if we, who already know many characters, are now asked to recognize incorrect characters, I dare not agree.

The first issue of the "Common Characters" vocabulary applies quite a few incorrect characters, and some of the "Common Characters" are not even popular incorrect characters. Even those of us who already know many characters do not recognize them. If this kind of "promotion" continues, and all kinds of magazines and books apply them in the future, I am afraid that even those of us who already know many characters will become illiterate. This is a major reason and justification for not daring to agree. Among them, writing "窮" (poor) as "穷," "懊" (annoyed) as "　," "讓" (allow) as "　," "腰" (waist) as "　," "塊" (chunk) as "块," etc., are all characters we do not recognize. Also, writing "從" (from) as "从" and "叢" (thicket) as "从" has already used one character for two purposes, making it impossible for people to distinguish them. Moreover, writing "麼" (question particle) as "　" is the same as the original standard character "　," which also feels inappropriate.

It is said that various magazines have published the first issue of the "Common Characters" vocabulary for a long time, but the reason for not printing the magazines in "Common Characters" is to first make people recognize the "Common Characters;" and it is also said that after two or three months, when everyone recognizes the "Common Characters," all magazines will be printed in "Common Characters." In this way, it means that we who already know many characters will become illiterate in these two or three months, and we should recognize the "imperial" vocabulary like elementary school students who are just beginning to learn to read.

For the sake of popularizing education and promoting culture, it is originally right for everyone to endure a little hardship; but it always seems unreasonable to us to ask everyone to endure hardship to recognize the non-popular characters used in "Common Characters." The "promotion" of "Common Characters" is a "middle way" of "simplifying the complex" and "choosing the easy over the difficult." Since it is an incomplete job and still requires everyone to endure hardship, I would rather recognize Latinized characters and have a thorough reform of the writing system.

The Universe Is Large Within the Pot 224

— Er Lang

In the writing room, A Gen was originally about to burst into flames. He came out and walked to the factory gate, and when he encountered the foreman, he glared at him and sneered. He couldn't bear it anymore. "Fuck your mother!" he shouted, and was about to pounce on him and beat him up, but he slipped away and went into the factory. A Da next door walked over, looking at him with strange eyes, and asked, "What's the matter?" A Gen met an acquaintance and couldn't help feeling a pang of grief, wanting to cry, but he held it back: crying is not for manly men. He lowered his head and answered him listlessly, "Fired." A Da was so surprised that his eyes turned white, and he asked again, "What's the matter?" He snorted, "That foreman pig," saying it unclearly, the fire of anger burning his head dizzy. A Da immediately remembered what happened yesterday.

Yesterday, A Gen and A Tai were working in the electrical room. A Zu often sighed, and A Da asked him, "What's the matter?" (A Da's "What's the matter?" had almost become his catchphrase, but in his environment, there were many things happening that made his catchphrase of "What's the matter?" impossible not to use). He was thinking, if the landlord always forces the rent, and last month because of illness, almost all of the wages were deducted! A Da sympathized. The two of them went from hating to cursing the factory. A Da had suffered before, and his words were not very激烈的。 A Gen didn't care about anything, cursing everyone and saying everything. Unbeknownst to them, the foreman was patrolling to the electrical room, and A Gen was exactly cursing the foreman pig. The foreman pressed his face close to his body, asking, "Who are you cursing? Fuck your mother!" and slapped him in the face. A Gen despised that pig the most, you hit me, good, he reached out and punched him. Although that pig was wearing a suit and looked like he had a strange martial spirit, but it was a silver-like wax spearhead, completely unable to withstand it, and A Gen gave him a light punch, and he fell into the coal pile. Groaning, he didn't dare to respond, and fled out of the electrical room in a mess...

Fired, what can I do? Although A Da sympathized, he had nothing to say, moreover, he was also suspected. He comforted A Gen for a while and went to the factory to work. A Gen lifted his dull and heavy feet, running around on the road. He passed the door of a small tavern, and the little girl inside selling songs, along with the stiff erhu, was singing "Ten Shouldn'ts". He made up his mind to spend the copper coins on his body on drinking, so he went into the tavern and sat down, put his right foot on the head of the stool, and called the waiter for four taels of white liquor. The couplet on the wall said, "The universe is large within the pot, the days are long in the barrel," he drank the wine and became a wine immortal.

A woman flashed past the door, holding a child in her arms who was gnawing on a big cake, dragging a dirty five or six-year-old child by the edge of her clothes. She glanced at A Gen and turned back to pace into the tavern. A Gen didn't expect it and was startled by her grab. The woman said, "Why aren't you going to work? You're able to float here, you dead drunk!" A Gen didn't open his mouth, only drinking his white liquor. The woman became even fiercer, "Dead drunk, you don't go to work today, you don't know that the landlord came to collect the rent, you're asking me to stand in the front, and you don't even want to think of a way? Drinking your life-shortening wine, where will we get rice for the night? You don't care about the big crying and the small shouting?..."

A Gen really wanted to take the opportunity to beat his wife up, but seeing the two little devils, big and small, next to him, thinking that from now on he would be fired, and the family didn't know what to do, eating the northwest wind? The more he thought about it, the more worried he became, and the woman's poisonous curses didn't blow into his ears...

Nun 225

— Tuo Ren

The green bamboo, spreading across the hillside, is as lush and green as if carved from jade. Within this jade-colored bamboo forest, the tips of red roofs are faintly revealed. During the day, the spring breeze rustles the tender green bamboo leaves, and the sound of the wooden fish, deep and resonant, drifts with the spring breeze into the ears of travelers on the road. When the sun sets in the west, the temple bell sounds like a lonely person's song in the wilderness, its tone somber and melancholy. This is a serene nunnery, forever spending its desolate years within this verdant bamboo forest.

When spring arrives, I think of the scenery in the warm breezes of the South. Especially, I am reminded of the tranquil "Emerald Bamboo Nunnery."

It must have been five years ago! I spent my days wandering through that emerald bamboo forest. At that time, I felt the transience of life and a sense of disgust for the social environment. I thought, I would also like to leave the reality of life and hide in the quiet mountains and forests, pursuing the sweetness of illusions, a peaceful dream. But after all, I didn't make the dream come true. I am still on life's journey in this realistic society, living a wandering life. Now, it has been five years. In these five years, I have not been fortunate enough to revisit that serene scenic spot, and I can only cherish the happy old dream of it in my imagination.

When I think of "Emerald Bamboo Nunnery," I think of Jing, the nun.

Jing, a young nun. Her youthful face showed a faint pallor, and her delicate dark eyebrows and clear eyes revealed a pensive sorrow. Her figure, her entire outline, revealed her to be a beautiful and serene woman. She often used silence to answer other people's questions, and she often used a smile to hide her sorrow. In the nunnery, she was a person who was loved by others, but she never showed affection for anyone.

Few people know her background. Although, from the outside, she must be a noble lady, and educated. But why did she become a nun? No one could guess.

One spring afternoon five years ago, I went to "Emerald Bamboo Nunnery" to play, and unintentionally, I noticed her. The reason I noticed her was also very accidental. When I walked behind the nunnery, wanting to go into the bamboo forest, I discovered her. At that time, she was sitting alone on the stone embankment of the ancient well. Immediately, I felt very strange: I felt that the nun must have some background. From that day on, the impression of her in my mind became stronger and stronger day by day.

Gradually, I got to know her. My curiosity was strong, so I often asked about her background, but her answer to me was silence. It seemed that all the words,

Page 21

were exhausted in that silence. After several disappointments, I stopped asking.

A few months later, I went home. Not many days after returning home, it was already high summer. In the morning sunlight, I received a very long letter from her, and one section of the letter read:

"...Perhaps you will be annoyed, why didn't I tell you my background? In fact, if you are angry because of this, then you are an ignorant person. You know that in this society, it is very easy for a woman to be destroyed. The reason I became a nun is because this society forced me to. The reason I don't tell people my background is also to preserve myself from being completely destroyed, that's why I remain silent... I don't believe in gods, but I want to be a nun. I am already ready to die, I already feel that life is tasteless, but I still want to live, this is my contradiction, and it can also be said to be the contradiction of society. I also understand that being a nun is not a good outcome, people can be destroyed, and nuns will also be poisoned one day..."

After receiving the letter, I realized that she was also a weak person under the evil forces of society, who would eventually be sacrificed.

Time passes quickly. It has been five years since receiving this letter. There has been no news from each other. I have been wandering in a foreign land for five years, and is she still existing in this society where the weak cannot survive?

That Fellow, Xiao Wang 226

— Xiao Qi

That fellow Xiao Wang has a long and crooked head, his cheekbones are high and upturned, his mouth is sharp, his skin color is as black and shiny as the asphalt used to pave roads, and his eyes dart around mischievously. His body is quite strong, and he doesn't mind walking long distances at all. His appearance is no different from a wild child roaming the streets, scavenging through trash cans for cigarette butts.

Does that rascal have any prospects? No. Although Xiao Wang is my fellow villager, I always look down on him, especially when he speaks, his awkwardness becomes even more vivid, making people find him repulsive and ridiculous.

Xiao Wang loves to gossip. When a group of guys are chatting idly, no matter what they are talking about, he always has a part to play. When people start talking about women, Xiao Wang becomes especially energetic, his protruding teeth showing as he grins, while he stutters and chatters:

— Hey, all you guys ever do is talk about love and stuff. You get weak in the knees when you see a woman. But… I've always looked down on that. What's so special about those girls? If you gave them to me, I'd have to think about it. With money, you can get any pretty girl you want. Hmph, what's so special about them? Right?

— Pshaw, Xiao Wang, don't talk big. Take a look in the mirror first. You wouldn't say no to any of them.

Someone needles Xiao Wang with a mocking tone. Xiao Wang doesn't blush. He knows he has an ugly face, but he has never blamed his parents for it, nor has he ever made a fuss about it. When people use this to tease him, Xiao Wang becomes proud instead:

— Hmph, that's not the way it works. I don't need to use a pretty-boy face to please the girls. My awkwardness makes the girls have to be nice to me. That's what's strange!

— Nobody believes you. Nobody believes your bragging, Xiao Wang.

— Gah! Xiao Wang, swear an oath then. Say, "If I, Xiao Wang, am bragging, may lightning strike me dead."

Then, Xiao Wang would launch into a story as if reciting it, babbling about when this girl treated him to a meal! When that girl gave him money to spend! By the end of the year, he could remember at least a dozen women whose pockets he had picked.

— Bragging, bragging. Xiao Wang, take a look in the mirror first.

Whether what Xiao Wang was saying was a lie or not, that's not important.

Xiao Wang never says anything serious all day long. He's always out and about, loafing around, and letting the days pass by. But he wears a coffee-colored Western suit that isn't too shabby, black leather shoes, and his tie is neatly tied. He smokes, goes to the movies from time to time, and eats at restaurants. He has never had a fixed residence of his own. Wherever he goes, that's where he is. Wherever he eats and stays, that's where he'll find it. No one knows exactly what line of work Xiao Wang does or how he makes his living. So you ask him:

— Xiao Wang, you don't work. How do you make a living?

— Of course I do. Although I don't work, I live quite comfortably.

Xiao Wang smiles, pride showing in his smile.

After he says that, you secretly feel that Xiao Wang is pretty good for nothing. He has no job, but he lives as leisurely as other people, and even more impressively. Where does he get it all from? Only Xiao Wang himself knows.

What exactly does Xiao Wang do? Even I can't figure it out. At the same time, I don't want to press him about it, because sometimes when I accidentally touch on this topic, he always seems hesitant to tell the truth. Sometimes I see that he doesn't have a cigarette in his mouth—cigarettes are as essential to him as rice. Then I understand that Xiao Wang is broke. But he has never asked me for half a cent. At most, he'll have a meal with you.

Xiao Wang has enormous courage, two thick legs, and a fist like a hammer. He doesn't care if someone hits him, but if he lands a punch on you, it's sure to hurt you in the back. It would be perfect to have Xiao Wang as a thug.

But I haven't seen Xiao Wang for a long time. I was wondering, and it happened that one day I ran into someone on the street who was often with Xiao Wang. He told me: Xiao Wang has been arrested for a few days.

"What for?" I asked in surprise.

"Only Xiao Wang himself knows."

The Story of Carrying the Donkey 227

— Xing An

Being a person is really difficult!

Being muddled-headed won't do: being serious is also not right.

Keeping oneself clean and good is individualism; going with the flow is being complicit in evil.

Being poor will be looked down upon; being rich will also be envied.

If you just get by, people will say you are living a life of drunken stupor; if you strive for progress, they will mock you for climbing up.

Revolution is for radicals; not revolution is for cold-blooded animals.

Wearing a queue and binding feet will of course be laughed at as being backward; wearing high hats and high-running shoes will inevitably be cursed as being trendy.

In short, nothing is satisfactory!

There is an Indian story that says: Once upon a time, there was an old man and a child who were using a donkey to carry goods to sell. After the goods were sold, the child rode the donkey, and the old man followed on foot, but passersby blamed him, saying that the child was ignorant for making an old man walk. So they switched places, with the old man riding the donkey and the child running behind. But others said the old man was heartless. The old man quickly hugged the child onto the saddle. Later, people who saw them said they were cruel for two people to be riding a donkey. So the old man and the child both got off. After walking for a while, others laughed at them, saying they were fools for not riding a perfectly good donkey. At this time, the old man sighed to the child, "We can't do it this way, and we can't do it that way. We only have one way left, and that is for the two of us to carry the donkey."

I think; the difficulty of being a person is sometimes as difficult as carrying a donkey!

Storytelling 230

Jiang Ruting, Zhu Jiesheng's Fallen Gold Fan

Zhonghua (1140) 9:00 PM to 9:45 PM

Opening: "Talent and Sentiment"

One part talent, one part sentiment, when talent is high, sentiment is also deep. Beautiful women invariably pity talented men, and talented men have always loved beautiful women. But then again, what's so hateful is why sentiment isn't evenly distributed. Thinking about the changes, sentiment isn't starting today, in the beginning, there were a lot of people who went through this. Some began with chaos and ended with abandonment, and some went from being enemies to being in-laws. One should know that Li Yi was heartless and forgot his previous promise, and Wang Kui betrayed his original alliance. You shouldn't learn from Song Hong, who didn't abandon his wife, or from Princess Lechang, who didn't remarry. It's not that human sentiment is thick or thin, it's just that talent is shallow or deep. You should know that dreaming of willows brings good matches, and poems written on leaves can also lead to marriage. It's ridiculous that worldly people are so lost and treat stealing jade and fragrance as proper, and that dew-like couples think things are right, leading to jealousy and quarrels, which is improper, and only causes disturbances. However, one can't avoid matters of love, and total friendship can be mistaken by some. As a result, those who can be moved should be moved.
