Shen Bao Local Supplement Movie Special

A Ludicrous Statement by Ida Cantor, Wife of Eddie Cantor 233

— Finch

Ida Cantor, wife of Eddie Cantor, the protagonist in "Congratulations," jumped up and exclaimed, "This is really annoying. If anyone asks me this again in the future, I'm going to scream!"

It turns out that everyone who sees the wife of this comedic master asks her, "Is he as funny at home as he is on the screen?" Ida said angrily, "For example, if your man is a bricklayer, or a chimney sweep, or a riding instructor, and people see you and constantly ask you, 'Does he always build walls at home? Can he paint flagpoles? Or does he ride horses in the living room?' How would you feel?"

"Oh, you wouldn't like it? I don't like it either. I married a real man who happens to be a comedian, not that I married a comedian who happens to be a man." Ida's statement is already quite humorous.

But Ida admitted that her husband is indeed very clever at home sometimes, but it's not pointless humor; it's deliberately done to make them laugh. She recalled one time when her husband came home from outside. He told her he was extremely tired and was going to take a nap. Ida and her five daughters then quietly stayed out of the way to let their father sleep. Eddie then went upstairs to sleep. After a while, Ida and her five daughters suddenly heard footsteps on the stairs. They looked back and saw Eddie walking down the stairs with his eyes closed, his hands outstretched in front of him, looking like he was sleepwalking, muttering, "It's too quiet at home. I'm sleepwalking. Someone make some noise to wake me up." He was wearing a top hat and a bathrobe. This astonished them all.

Ida said, "Indeed, he often plays the fool at home, especially when we have some quarrels or disagreements. These little things are unavoidable in even the best families, but when Eddie finds out, he tries to make us laugh and make everyone happy. In Eddie's mind, the family is the center of his universe. The reason he can be funny on screen is because he is happy at home."

Ida then talked about the time before she married this comedic star: "I've known him for a long time. I knew him when he was still wearing short pants. Those short pants weren't for playing golf. Back then, when a group of kids were playing under the subway stairs, if anyone mentioned golf, we would definitely think he had eaten too many turnips. We went to school together at Henry Street Elementary School back then. I admired his cleverness and humor very much, so we were particularly close. He often walked with me and carried my schoolbag. He still often says, 'I used to carry your textbooks, but now you carry my bankbooks.'"

It turns out that Eddie Cantor once worked as a tailor. This was also revealed by his wife. He became a tailor because of her. Because after Eddie went on stage and played the fool, they began to talk about marriage. But Ida's family opposed her marrying a stage clown. Therefore, Eddie abandoned the path indicated by his talent and left the stage. He looked for many other jobs, and one of them was working as a tailor at a clothing company. But he was soon fired by the owner because he unknowingly cut good fabric into many little dancing figures.

From then on, he did many other jobs. For a whole year, he repented and wanted to be an ordinary person, clearing out the singing and dancing in his blood, but in the end, he was unsuccessful. "So I gave in," said Ida Cantor. "Although he still insisted on being a 'gentleman' to please my family, I knew he couldn't go against his talent and his heart. So I decided to call him back to the stage. I also resolved to marry him regardless of my family's opinions. So I didn't marry him because he was a comedian, but because he was the only person I admired, whether he was a comedian or not. Until now, my decision has been infinitely rewarded."

Film Review

### Review of "The Golden Lotus Tragedy" 234

— Warren

Have A Heart - Shown in Nanjing

In literature, many works have succeeded in depicting the tragedy and comedy of physical defects and disabilities. This is not only because people with psychological abnormalities have rich processes and phenomena that can be described, but also because the people involved have extremely deep inner sorrow due to certain defects, making it easier to write something touching?

"The Golden Lotus Tragedy," as the translated title indicates, is about a tragedy enacted by a young lady due to her unfortunate foot. The author uses the female protagonist Sally's teaching of dancing to implant in the audience's mind the impression of her beautiful, colorful, delicate, and lively movements. Then, he uses the pre-wedding revelry to maintain the joyful atmosphere of the drama at a considerable level. Then, abruptly, due to a misstep in the joy, she fell and became physically disabled. This turned the plot into a tragedy. Moreover, the fact that her fiancé no longer loved her because of her misfortune won the audience's sympathy for her and maintained the mood of meticulously depicting her life thereafter.

The plot unfolds in Sally's loving life with Jim, a candy and ice cream company salesman, depicting how she tries to hide her flaws, how he happens to discover them, and how, on the contrary, Jim loves her even more because she has suffered this regret. These are the ups and downs and twists and turns of the play. In fact, if the playwright could have found a way to end it here, it would still have been a good script. However, he dragged out the plot unnecessarily with a chance occurrence, dragging the plot into a detective case, with Jim being wrongly accused of being a thief and imprisoned, and Sally redeeming him with money, only for him to leave in anger, doing these simply superfluous scenes. The author was also afraid that this would make the audience impatient, so he used intense actions such as horse racing and catching the real thief as stimulation. Then he let Jim run to Sally, whose foot disease had been cured but who was disheartened, to rekindle the flames of love, completing a happy ending.

Such a plot, while gaining so-called twists and turns, inevitably becomes a mediocre tune.

Director David Butler's handling of this film is quite commendable. At the beginning, only a few simple scenes depicted Sally's life and personality very vividly and deeply. The atmosphere of the pre-wedding night was also quite sufficient. In Sally's dialogue and expressions with the doctor, and her special attention to her feet when making toy idols, Jim's sudden visit and her desire to hide her sick foot but being unable to do so, a few short shots portrayed the mood of a girl with a physical defect extremely well. Secondly, the appearance of children and dogs in the play is also very appropriate and effective. The former shows Sally teaching a large group of children to dance at the beginning, and the group of children surrounding and cheering when she and her lover Joey go out. Before she meets her second lover, Jim, while sitting at the window with a disability, a group of street children surround Jim buying candy and singing along with him, which makes for a powerful correspondence before and after. The latter, the several appearances of this little dog, serve as a companion to the heroine's sorrow and as an important thing in her memories or connections.

From her debut in "Little Women" to starring in this "Golden Lotus Tragedy," Joan Bennett has achieved a very pleasing result. Her pretty thin face and figure, as well as her portrayal of the mood of a girl with a physical defect and unspeakable pain in her life, are particularly moving. James Dunn, who plays Jim, is rugged, and Una Merkel, who plays her friend Joan, is a bit straightforward, and her sentimentality is a fitting and contrasting portrayal.

### Review of "The Wife's Lover" 235

— Ji Han

Hat Coat Glove

— Shown at the Great Shanghai Theater —

Changing the title "Hat, Coat, Gloves" to "The Wife's Lover" not only has a seductive effect on business appeal, but also explains the husband's sadness, which is the main part of the play, in the title. Yes, if "The Wife's Lover" can move married people, it is because the lawyer Robert discovers that his wife is having an affair but cannot ignore the dignity between husband and wife. In this kind of place, capitalist writers, in literature and in drama, often depict it as a contradiction between emotion and reason.

It is said that this film is adapted from a stage play. If the original play was a five-act play, then the first act would be the husband and wife and the wife's lover buying hats, coats, gloves, etc. in Shangtang, the second act would be the husband having dinner at his wife's house and hearing his wife talking on the phone with her lover, the third act would be the wife's lover - the young painter - wearing the husband's old coat at the wife's house, the fourth act would be the young painter leaving his model and the model's accidental death, and the fifth act would be the court.

Of course, I have not seen the original script. This is just a guess based on what I saw in the movie. However, if my guess is not too wrong, then the traces of the stage play in the movie "The Wife's Lover" are easy to find. Everyone knows that the superiority of movies is that they are not limited by time and space. However, Madame Dubarry's sudden testimony in court is the original-like application of the stage play, because in the stage play, Madame Dubarry's house cannot be a separate act, but in the movie, it is not necessary to do so. The heaviness of the dialogue is also too much cherishing of the original play. So much dialogue is annoying in the movie no matter what. What remains to be said is that the so-called "no coincidence, no play" is almost entirely organized by coincidence here. Therefore, people cannot help but feel that this is acting, and there will never be such coincidences in the world.

Apart from writing about the so-called sadness of the husband losing his wife's love, there is almost nothing commendable in the play. And in capitalist society, love disputes between husband and wife are so ordinary! However, American films often feel great interest in this area. Even more mediocre is that here, like ordinary comedies and tragedies, there will inevitably be a reunion.

From the court scene to the scene of the painter's model's accidental death, it can be seen that the director worked very hard. The model's crazy transformation after being heartbroken, contrasting with the lawyer's shared fate, certainly brings out the emotions of the play, and the various things in the court are not stagnant or dull, which is even more commendable. In particular, the laughable and coy demeanor of Madame Dubarry is used as an interesting interlude, which can make the atmosphere lively and vivid. As for the plaintiff lawyer's clever arguments, contrasting with the defendant lawyer's rebuttal of all the evidence, this implies that the law of our capitalist society is really too childish, although the author's original intention was not this. However, Ricarco Cortez's sentimental acting skills make this ordinary film work much more colorful.

### "The Escape" Will Be Released Today 236

— Qingyun

The great production of Yihua Company this year, "The Escape," a music and song film filmed on location in Mongolia, Chahar, and Suiyuan, has been decided to be released today (23rd) at the Jincheng Grand Theater. The main purpose of this film is to expose the miserable situation of the enemy oppressing our Chinese nation, the evil deeds of those who are not human, and the ugly faces of hypocrites who use public welfare as a name to collect money for their own benefit. At the same time, it vividly depicts on the screen the plight of the refugee people who have been occupied by the enemy and have no home to return to. The plot is realistic, the performance is exciting and tense, and the two songs interspersed in the film, "The Escape Song" and "Song of the Village Girl in the North," are also extremely tragic, heroic, and listenable. Other aspects such as directing, photography, and scenery are also beautifully achieved. Art-loving friends, "The Escape" is really a masterpiece not to be missed.

The Soviet Embassy Presents "The Arctic Expedition Disaster" 237

In order to promote Sino-Russian cultural communication and introduce its films, the Soviet Embassy in China specially invited people from all walks of life in China and abroad to visit the Soviet film "Arctic Heroes" ("Heraos of the Arctic") at the Capital National Grand Theater on the evening of the 20th of this month. More than a thousand guests attended, all of whom expressed satisfaction with the film and praised it. However, the guests that evening entered the venue with invitations, causing many viewers to feel regretful. In response to the enthusiastic requests from all walks of life, the National Grand Theater obtained the consent of the Soviet Embassy to publicly screen the film for several days from the 20th to share the fun. The theater has been packed every day, and the value of the film can be imagined. It is heard that as soon as the film is finished screening in Nanjing, it will meet with the people of Shanghai.

Movie Novel

Clive of India (7) 238

— Mao De

Soon they had another son. They felt that their life was so fulfilling that it could be considered unparalleled. Although Little Clive's physique was very weak, the King of England sent the royal physician, Sir Foulis, to diagnose and treat the child, so they felt that he would soon grow up strong and that tragedy and worry would never befall them.

Although Clive was a soldier, his active and combative nature was not suitable for living in peace. Therefore, he soon wanted to occupy a high position in the domestic officialdom. After military service, warriors often like to dabble in civil affairs, and Clive could not escape this custom. So he joined the election competition for members of parliament. In this election, he seized a huge amount of wealth, wanting to occupy a seat in the parliament. He felt that once he could join the ranks of the parliamentarians, he could fulfill his human duties for the country, for the family, and for himself.

But at this time, disturbances occurred in India again. The new ruler of India, Salaudtudola, colluded with the French and wanted to drive British merchants out of India. At this time, British merchants in India thought of a person again, a warrior who could turn defeat into victory and defeat the enemy with few soldiers. But how could they get his help? The board of directors of the East India Trading Company was holding an important meeting in London at this time. Chairman Sullivan said: "But he is already rich now. Why would he be willing to do that kind of thing? Moreover, he has recently had considerable success in the parliamentary election. He also has a lovely wife and young children. How can we trick him into going back to India?"

One of the resourceful directors, Zhuang Qidong, said: "It is certainly not feasible to trick him out, but we can use a trick to make him willing to come out himself. He is not from a wealthy family, but his behavior is extravagant, no less than a prince. In the election, he has spent almost all his wealth. We only need to find some minor problems in the technical details to prevent him from entering the parliament, then wouldn't he have wasted a lot of money in vain? At that time, we will propose conditions to him. Not only will he have to accept them, but he will also be grateful to us."

Tragedy and worry did come to the home of Clive and Lady Margaret. It was a tragedy that almost neither Margaret Clive nor any woman could bear. One day, Lord Foulis told her that her son had no hope of survival. That might be in a few months, but that was beyond human help. The result was inevitable, but it was only a matter of time. She was feeling grief after hearing the doctor's words, when Clive came back from outside. He said that the position he had won in Parliament had been taken away by others. He sat in his usual chair, holding his head in his hands, the veins on his head bulging. His old head wound always flared up whenever things didn't go his way.

Margaret stood behind him, slowly stroking his head, sprinkling cool medicine on his head from time to time. She was thinking sadly, how could she let him know what the doctor had said? But could she bear these heavy sorrows alone?

After a while, Clive felt calmer and said, "Margaret, your hands are so strange. I think if I didn't have you, what fun would there be in the world?" After a while, he said again, "Margaret, our family is ruined!" Margaret sat down on the small stool next to him and said, "Indeed, I know. But from now on, we can have you at home more often, because..." (To be continued)

Correction: The novel "Clive of India" published on the 20th was paragraph 4, mistakenly made into paragraph 5. The 21st was paragraph 5, mistakenly made into paragraph 6. The 22nd was paragraph 6, mistakenly made into paragraph 7. This is hereby corrected.
